- [x] SEC-H116. **Customer merge type-coercion guard.** Pre-fix: `POST /customers/merge` at `packages/server/src/routes/customers.routes.ts:451` compared `keep_id === merge_id` using the raw `req.body` values. JS `===` is type-strict, so `{keep_id: "5", merge_id: 5}` bypassed the self-merge check ŌĆö the downstream `Number(keep_id)` / `Number(merge_id)` coercion then collapsed both to `5`, and the handler ran every UPDATE with `customer_id=mid`/`WHERE customer_id=mid` against the same row plus a final `UPDATE customers SET is_deleted=1 WHERE id=mid` ŌĆö soft-deleting the only customer. Post-fix: compute `kid = Number(keep_id)` / `mid = Number(merge_id)` ONCE at the top, gate on `Number.isFinite + Number.isInteger + > 0` (rejects NaN, Infinity, floats, negatives, zero) with `400 'keep_id and merge_id must be positive integers'`, then compare `kid === mid` in the coerced space for the self-merge guard. Both SELECTs and every downstream UPDATE now use the already-validated `kid`/`mid` locals (removed the redundant `Number()` re-coercion in the SELECTs). Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ exit 0 (zero errors). Grep confirms `keep_id === merge_id` gone and new `kid === mid` + `Number.isFinite` guard present at lines 453-456. Files modified: `packages/server/src/routes/customers.routes.ts` (+5/-4). (LOGIC-008)

- [x] SEC-H60. **HMAC-signed backup metadata sidecar + slug/tenant_id binding for restore integrity.** Pre-fix: `packages/server/src/services/backup.ts` encrypted each backup as `<slug>-t<tenantId>-<ts>-<rand>.db.enc` (AES-256-GCM via `encryptFile`), but restore only validated (a) the filename matched the `isBackupFile` regex + path-traversal guard, (b) AES-GCM decrypt succeeded, and (c) `PRAGMA integrity_check` came back `ok`. An attacker (or operator with shared NAS access) who could drop a file into the backup directory could swap tenant A's `.db.enc` into tenant B's slot, name it `bizarre-crm-<matching-ts>-<rand>.db.enc`, and `POST /admin/backups/:filename/restore` would happily decrypt it (both encrypted with the shared `BACKUP_ENCRYPTION_KEY` so the AES-GCM tag verifies), integrity-check it (tenant A's DB is a valid SQLite file), safety-backup tenant B's current DB, and overwrite tenant B with tenant A's data ŌĆö a cross-tenant data substitution with no explicit forgery primitive required. Post-fix: (a) **`config.backupMetadataKey`** new env var `BACKUP_METADATA_KEY` (optional; Ōēź32 chars); when unset, derived via `crypto.hkdfSync('sha256', JWT_SECRET||BACKUP_ENCRYPTION_KEY, salt='bizarre-backup-meta-salt-v1', info='backup-metadata-hmac-v1-fallback', 32)` in `services/backup.ts:getSidecarKey()` with a prod-mode operator warning about the rotation coupling. Raw env var path uses info `'backup-metadata-hmac-v1'` so the key space is domain-separated from the fallback. (b) **Sidecar format** ŌĆö `writeBackupMetadata()` writes `<backup-file>.meta.json` containing `{slug, tenant_id, backup_version: 1, written_at: ISO-8601, hmac: hex(HMAC-SHA256(key, `${slug}|${tenant_id}|${backup_version}|${written_at}`))}`. Canonical input string lives in `canonicalSidecarInput()`; changing the order/separator requires bumping `METADATA_VERSION` so old sidecars don't silently re-verify under new semantics. (c) **runBackup() integration** ŌĆö after `encryptFile()` returns the final path, the sidecar is written with `opts.tenantSlug || 'bizarre-crm'` + `opts.tenantId ?? 0` (single-tenant uses stable placeholders so the verification contract stays uniform). A sidecar-write failure logs loud but doesn't fail the backup ŌĆö the ciphertext is still on disk and usable via `--allow-unsigned`; the restore handler will refuse unless the operator opts in. (d) **restoreBackup() integration** ŌĆö new required `RestoreBackupOptions` fields `expectedSlug` + `expectedTenantId` + optional `allowUnsigned`. Three-layer verify: (i) cheap filename-prefix check via new `extractSlugFromBackupFilename()` ŌĆö returns `bizarre-crm` for single-tenant and the `<slug>` portion of `<slug>-t<id>-...` for multi-tenant, rejects mismatch before touching crypto; (ii) `verifyBackupMetadata()` reads the sidecar, rejects on malformed JSON / missing fields / wrong `backup_version`, recomputes HMAC and compares with `crypto.timingSafeEqual(providedBuf, expectedBuf)` (length-equalised to avoid the TSE length mismatch throw), then binds `slug === expectedSlug` + `tenant_id === expectedTenantId`; (iii) `ENOENT` on sidecar path counts as `unsigned: true` and is only accepted when caller passes `allowUnsigned: true` ŌĆö any OTHER sidecar read failure (EACCES, corrupt JSON, HMAC mismatch, wrong tenant) hard-rejects regardless. Logged reasons: `Sidecar does not exist`, `Sidecar JSON malformed`, `Sidecar is missing required fields`, `Unsupported sidecar version`, `Sidecar HMAC mismatch ŌĆö file may have been tampered with`, `Sidecar slug "X" does not match target tenant "Y"`, `Sidecar tenant_id N does not match target tenant_id M`. (e) **admin.routes.ts `/admin/backups/:filename/restore` threading** ŌĆö expectedSlug/expectedTenantId hardcoded to `'bizarre-crm'` / `0` (admin panel is single-tenant; multi-tenant mode kill-switch at line 233 already blocks it). `allowUnsigned = req.body?.allow_unsigned === true` so the UI must explicitly send the flag. Audit events `admin_backup_restore_start` + `admin_backup_restore_failed` + `admin_backup_restore_success` now carry `allowUnsigned` + `unsigned` details so log review can distinguish "refused because unsigned and no opt-in" from "verified sidecar pass". HTTP status: 400 for user-correctable errors (wrong tenant/unsigned/tamper) vs 500 for server faults ŌĆö the UI can toast the tamper case differently from "disk full". (f) **pruneBackups() + deleteBackup() sidecar cleanup** ŌĆö both now `unlink(dbFile + METADATA_SUFFIX)` alongside the backup, preventing orphan `.meta.json` files from accumulating in the backup dir and masquerading as integrity evidence for a non-existent backup. (g) **Back-compat**: pre-SEC-H60 backups have no sidecar ŌåÆ `unsigned: true` ŌåÆ refused by default ŌåÆ operator must send `allow_unsigned=true` in the POST body to restore. New backups from this build forward carry sidecars and pass the default restore path. Dev/single-tenant uses `bizarre-crm`/`0` placeholders so existing `runBackup()` callers that don't pass tenantSlug/tenantId keep working. (h) **Verified**: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ zero errors. Files modified: `packages/server/src/config.ts` (+22 lines: `backupMetadataKey` getter + prod-mode warning); `packages/server/src/services/backup.ts` (+~170 lines: sidecar constants, `getSidecarKey()` with HKDF fallback, `canonicalSidecarInput()`, `computeSidecarHmac()`, `writeBackupMetadata()`, `verifyBackupMetadata()`, `extractSlugFromBackupFilename()`, runBackup sidecar-write block, restoreBackup filename + HMAC + tenant verify block, prune/delete sidecar cleanup); `packages/server/src/routes/admin.routes.ts` (+~30 lines: expectedSlug/expectedTenantId wiring, allow_unsigned body parse, status-400-vs-500 branching, audit payload extensions). Note: the original task description referenced `super-admin.routes.ts:1161-1183` but that line range is actually the 2FA force-disable endpoint (`POST /tenants/:slug/users/:userId/2fa/force-disable`) ŌĆö no restore endpoint lives in super-admin.routes.ts. Backup restore is served only from `admin.routes.ts:/backups/:filename/restore` which is explicitly blocked in multi-tenant mode (the kill-switch middleware at line 233 returns 403 for any admin path except `/login` + `/terminate-tenant`), so the single-tenant admin route is the only surface that needed the verification threaded through it. Commit a505fbe. (P3-PII-17, 18)

- [x] SEC-H57. **Retention rules for sms_messages / call_logs / email_messages / ticket_notes (24-month default, tenant-configurable).** Pre-fix: four customer-communications tables were unbounded growth. `sms_messages`, `call_logs`, `email_messages` were appended-to on every inbound/outbound text, call, and email but nothing ever trimmed them; `ticket_notes` carried every internal diagnostic/email/customer-reply typed against a ticket for the life of the database. `services/retentionSweeper.ts` already ran a 2-AM-local-per-tenant cron over eight ops-log tables (automation_run_log, webhook_delivery_failures, rate_limits, sms_retry_queue, notification_queue, notification_retry_queue, report_snapshots, import_rate_limits) but had no coverage for PII comms. GDPR / CCPA / most US state privacy regimes require a stated retention purpose for customer-communications data ŌĆö indefinite storage is not defensible. P3-PII-08 wanted 24 months as the small-business baseline (matches RepairDesk / Shopify / Square defaults) with per-tenant override via `store_config`. Post-fix: (a) **Migration `108_pii_retention_defaults.sql`** ŌĆö adds `redacted_at TEXT` and `redacted_by INTEGER REFERENCES users(id)` columns to `ticket_notes`, plus a partial index `idx_ticket_notes_redaction_pending ON ticket_notes(created_at) WHERE redacted_at IS NULL` so the nightly sweep stays cheap even on shops with millions of notes (once a row is redacted it drops out of the index permanently). Seeds four `store_config` keys at the 24mo default via `INSERT OR IGNORE`: `retention_sms_months`, `retention_calls_months`, `retention_email_months`, `retention_ticket_notes_months`. Idempotent ŌĆö running on a tenant that already has any of the keys is a no-op. (b) **`services/retentionSweeper.ts` PII phase** ŌĆö separate from the existing `RULES` array because (1) the unit is months, not days, so humans writing a privacy policy aren't doing `24*30` math in their head, (2) the window is per-tenant config in `store_config`, not a hardcoded literal, and (3) `ticket_notes` uses REDACT semantics, not DELETE. New `PiiRule` interface + `PII_RULES` array: sms_messages / call_logs / email_messages in `mode: 'delete'`, ticket_notes in `mode: 'redact'` with `redactColumn: 'content'`. (c) **Delete path** (sms/calls/emails): plain `DELETE FROM <table> WHERE created_at < datetime('now', '-<N> months')` ŌĆö the row IS the record, redacting just the body leaves an orphan nobody can use. (d) **Redact path** (ticket_notes): `UPDATE ticket_notes SET content = '', redacted_at = datetime('now') WHERE created_at < <cutoff> AND redacted_at IS NULL`. Keeps the row because `ticket_notes.parent_id` is a self-FK (deleting a parent would cascade-orphan replies) and because the audit trail (who/when/which ticket) has operational value even after the body is gone. The `redacted_at IS NULL` guard makes the redact idempotent ŌĆö already-redacted rows cost only an index probe on subsequent sweeps. (e) **`readPiiRetentionMonths()`** ŌĆö clamps the config value to `[MIN_PII_MONTHS=1, MAX_PII_MONTHS=120]` (1 month to 10 years) so a fat-fingered admin setting of "0" cannot wipe the entire table on the next run ("older than 0 months ago" = everything) and "99999" cannot silently disable the sweep through SQLite's datetime overflow behavior. `Number.isFinite` + parseInt + `< MIN` all fall back to the 24mo default; `> MAX` clamps to 120. (f) **`columnExists()` guard** on the redact path ŌĆö if migration 108 hasn't been applied to this tenant yet (fresh tenant mid-provision, or post-restore reconciliation before re-migrate), the PII sweep skips the ticket_notes rule silently rather than half-redacting without the timestamp. Next sweep picks it up automatically once the column exists. (g) **`writeRetentionAudit()`** ŌĆö emits one `audit_logs` row per non-zero batch with `event = 'retention_sweep_pii'` and `details` JSON carrying `{table, mode, rows_affected, retention_months, ran_at}`. Compliance gets a paper trail without a row-per-deleted-row explosion (a shop with 500k stale SMS rows would otherwise generate a 500k-row audit explosion on the first sweep). Audit write failures are swallowed with an error log so they cannot abort the remaining PII rules ŌĆö the sweep already did the underlying work, losing the breadcrumb is recoverable. (h) **Phase ordering** ŌĆö PII phase runs AFTER the ops-log phase so a failure in the ops sweep cannot skip the (arguably more important) compliance-driven PII retention. Each PII rule runs in its own `try/catch` for the same isolation reason as the ops loop. (i) **No new cron** ŌĆö the existing 2-AM-local-per-tenant retention-sweep cron in `index.ts:2173-2220` calls `runRetentionSweep()` which now does both phases in sequence. No wiring changes needed. Inherits the existing `circuitAllowsRun` / `recordCircuitFailure` / `shouldRunDaily` guardrails so a misbehaving PII sweep on one tenant won't cascade into a fleet-wide failure. (j) **Spot-check verified** against in-memory SQLite: seeded 2 rows per PII table (one 30 months old, one 1 month old) with `retention_*_months=24`; post-sweep: 1 row remaining per delete-mode table (the recent one), 2 rows remaining in ticket_notes but 1 with `redacted_at IS NOT NULL` + `content = ''` (content blanked, row intact for FK), 4 `retention_sweep_pii` audit breadcrumbs written, `totalDeleted=4`, no cross-table data loss. Typecheck: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ zero errors (exit 0). Files: `packages/server/src/db/migrations/108_pii_retention_defaults.sql` (new, 50 lines), `packages/server/src/services/retentionSweeper.ts` (+213/-13: new `PiiRule` interface, `PII_RULES` array, `readPiiRetentionMonths`/`columnExists`/`writeRetentionAudit`/`applyPiiRule` helpers, second sweep loop in `runRetentionSweep`). Ships as two commits (migration and sweeper landed separately due to a worktree race with a parallel SEC-H54 task that was modifying adjacent files): commits 08d6b9c (migration) and 0a4e1f1 (sweeper code). (P3-PII-08)

- [x] SEC-H54. **Gate `/uploads/<slug>/*` behind auth; HMAC-signed URLs for portal/MMS; separate `/admin-uploads` for super-admin artefacts.** Pre-fix: `app.use('/uploads', (req, res, next) => { ... express.static(basePath, { dotfiles: 'deny', index: false }) })` at `packages/server/src/index.ts:1141-1161` served every file under `config.uploadsPath/<tenantSlug>/...` (or `config.uploadsPath/...` in single-tenant mode) to any caller with the URL. Filenames are 32-hex random strings generated by `fileUploadValidator` so the primary exposure was information-disclosure via URL leakage ŌĆö browser-history sync to the user's personal phone, email clients that render `<img src="/uploads/...">` and proxy images through their own CDNs, screenshot+forward chains, server-log forwarding that includes full request paths, and any place a logged-in user pastes a URL thinking only the shop sees it. More importantly, a cross-tenant leak (a URL from tenant A rendered inside tenant B's support screen, or simply guessed by an attacker with knowledge of another tenant's slug) served whatever that URL pointed at with zero check that the caller even held a valid session for that tenant. Post-fix: (a) **`config.uploadsSecret`** added to `packages/server/src/config.ts` reading `UPLOADS_SECRET` env var. Mirrors the existing `jwtSecret` shape ŌĆö FATAL-exit in production when missing/insecure/<32 chars, warning in dev with a derived `dev-uploads-secret-${JWT_SECRET.slice(0,16)}` fallback so local smoke tests work without editing `.env`. Distinct from JWT_SECRET so a JWT leak doesn't hand out signed-URL minting. (b) **`config.adminUploadsPath`** set to `packages/server/data/admin-uploads/` ŌĆö separate directory under `data/` (not inside `uploads/`) so the normal upload multer handlers cannot accidentally land here. `utils/startupValidation.ts` creates it on boot alongside the regular uploads dir. (c) **New utility `packages/server/src/utils/signedUploads.ts`** ŌĆö exports `signUploadUrl(slug, file, ttlSeconds = 3600, type = 'uploads')` and `verifySignedUpload(type, slug, file, exp, sig)`. Signature scheme: `canonical = \`${type}|${slug}|${file}|${exp}\`` (pipe-delimited; filenames are multer-generated hex and never contain pipes), `sig = HMAC-SHA256(uploadsSecret, canonical).base64url`. URL shape: `/signed-url/${type}/${slug}/${encodeURIComponent(file)}?exp=${unixSeconds}&sig=${sig}`. TTL clamped to `[60s, 7d]` so callers can't mint trivially-short or pseudo-permanent URLs. `verifySignedUpload` narrows to `{ok: true}` or `{ok: false, reason: 'expired'|'bad_signature'|'malformed'}` so the handler can emit the correct HTTP code ŌĆö `410 Gone` for expired (the URL was valid, it just timed out) and `403 Forbidden` for bad-sig/malformed. Constant-time compare via `crypto.timingSafeEqual` on same-length `Buffer`s with a pre-check on length to avoid the comparator's throw. `type` distinguishes subdirectory convention (`uploads|mms|recordings|bench|shrinkage|inventory`) so the same signing primitive serves every upload surface without special-cases in the verifier. (d) **`/uploads/*` handler (`index.ts:1141-1163`)** ŌĆö added `authMiddleware` before the path-resolution block. `req.tenantSlug` is set by `tenantResolver`; `authMiddleware` already rejects requests whose JWT `tenantSlug` mismatches `req.tenantSlug` (cross-tenant token-reuse block from existing hardening). `basePath` = `config.uploadsPath + (req.tenantSlug ? '/' + req.tenantSlug : '')`, path traversal blocked via `path.resolve` + `startsWith(basePath)`. `express.static` serves the resolved file with `dotfiles: 'deny', index: false`. (e) **`/signed-url/:type/:slug/:file`** ŌĆö regex route `/^\/signed-url\/([^/]+)\/([^/]+)\/(.+)$/` so the file can contain slashes (nested uploads under `bench/qc-signatures/` etc.). NO auth middleware ŌĆö the signature IS the auth. Verifier runs first; on success, file resolution runs under `config.uploadsPath/<slug>/[<type>/]<file>` with the same `path.resolve` traversal guard as the auth-gated path. Even after signature success, `..`/`\\` are rejected as a defence-in-depth guard for the case where `uploadsSecret` leaks and a forged signature tries to climb out of the tenant directory. (f) **`/admin-uploads/*`** ŌĆö inline handler at `index.ts` chaining `localhostOnly` + super-admin JWT verify (borrowing the exact verify options from `super-admin.routes.ts`: `{algorithms:['HS256'], issuer:'bizarre-crm', audience:'bizarre-crm-super-admin'}`, role must equal `'super_admin'`). Serves from `config.adminUploadsPath`, same `dotfiles: 'deny'` + path-resolve guard. No tenant namespace here ŌĆö super-admin artefacts are operator-owned, not tenant-owned, so files live flat under the directory. (g) **`.env.example`** documents `UPLOADS_SECRET` with the standard `node -e "console.log(require('crypto').randomBytes(32).toString('hex'))"` recipe. (h) **Not yet migrated**: existing upload call sites (`bench.routes.ts:829-972`, `inventory.routes.ts:910-911`, `inventoryEnrich.routes.ts:679-680`, `settings.routes.ts:1459-1460`, `sms.routes.ts:409,839`, `voice.routes.ts:413`) still write relative `/uploads/...` strings into the DB. In-app consumers (React app) already hit these via the same session that authMiddleware accepts, so no client change was needed for the primary web surface; however, outbound public contexts (email receipt images, MMS media URLs, portal approval attachments) must flip to `signUploadUrl(...)` when that sender code next gets touched. Follow-up items tracked as separate TODOs at each call site ŌĆö out of scope for this ticket, which closes the *serving* gap. (i) **Verified**: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ zero errors. Files: `packages/server/src/config.ts` (+34, uploadsSecret + adminUploadsPath), `packages/server/src/utils/signedUploads.ts` (new, 113 lines), `packages/server/src/utils/startupValidation.ts` (+10, admin-uploads dir create), `packages/server/src/index.ts` (+100/-17: jwt import, auth-gated /uploads, /signed-url handler, /admin-uploads handler), `.env.example` (+7, UPLOADS_SECRET doc block). Commit 7cb27c4. (P3-PII-07 / PUB-022)

- [x] SEC-H55. **Audit `customer_viewed` on GET `/:id` + bulk list-with-stats with 5-minute coalescing.** Pre-fix: two PII-accessing read paths in `packages/server/src/routes/customers.routes.ts` produced zero audit rows. (a) `GET /:id` at line 991 fetched a full customer row (names, email, phone, mobile, address, SMS opt-in state, comments, tax number, plus denormalized ticket_count + total_invoiced + RFM computation) and returned everything to the caller without touching `audit_logs`. (b) `GET /` at line 88 (the list-with-stats endpoint when `?include_stats=1` is set, and the primary directory surface even without stats) paged through every customer in the tenant with the same PII-rich `c.*` projection ŌĆö a single staff account could scroll the entire customer base with no forensic trail. P3-PII-05 wanted both paths audited so a later insider-threat review could answer "who viewed customer X between Tue 2pm and 4pm" from `audit_logs` alone. Post-fix: (1) **New helper `packages/server/src/utils/customerViewAudit.ts`** ŌĆö exports `shouldAuditCustomerView(key: string, now?: number): boolean` backed by a module-scoped `Map<string, number>` that records the last-audit timestamp per key. Returns true (write the row) when no entry exists or the entry is older than `COALESCE_WINDOW_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000`; otherwise returns false. Map-size safety: `MAX_ENTRIES = 5000` triggers a two-pass sweep ŌĆö first evict anything already outside the window, then if still over cap drop the oldest half by insertion order (JS `Map` preserves insertion order per spec). Self-evicting on access keeps hot keys fresh and cold keys decaying naturally; an unbounded Map would otherwise accumulate one entry per (user, filter-fingerprint, page) tuple indefinitely on a long-lived process. Test hook `__resetCustomerViewAuditCacheForTests()` clears the cache so unit tests can scope state per-case. In-memory, per-process ŌĆö a restart drops the window (acceptable: the first post-restart view always writes) and multi-process deployments each keep their own window (acceptable: worst case N rows per window across N processes, not N-per-view). (2) **`GET /:id` instrumentation** (lines 1060-1070 area) ŌĆö after the RFM health-score computation finishes and immediately before the `res.json`, builds `viewCoalesceKey = \`${userId ?? 'anon'}:get-by-id:${id}\`` and, when `shouldAuditCustomerView` returns true, calls `audit(req.db, 'customer_viewed', userId, req.ip || 'unknown', { via: 'get-by-id', tenant: req.tenantSlug ?? null, customer_id: id })`. Refreshing the detail page a dozen times inside 5 min writes exactly one row; waiting past the window and returning writes a fresh row. (3) **`GET /` instrumentation** (right after the `customers.map` that adds `profile_completeness`/`missing_fields`) ŌĆö writes ONE row per page instead of one row per customer, carrying `customer_ids: [...]` in details. The task spec's "consider batching ŌĆö one row per PAGE with `{customer_ids: [...]}`" trade-off was chosen: a 250-row page (`pageSize` max) would otherwise produce 250 audit rows per scan; 250 rows compressed into a single JSON array stays well under the 16KB `MAX_AUDIT_DETAILS_BYTES` cap in `utils/audit.ts` while preserving the forensic "who saw which ids" link. Coalesce key is `${userId ?? 'anon'}:list-with-stats:${filterFingerprint}` where `filterFingerprint` is a deterministic JSON of `{kw, gid, sort, stats, from, to, open, off, ps}` ŌĆö the same filters produce the same fingerprint and coalesce, changing filters or scrolling to a new page produces a different fingerprint so the new page writes a fresh row (as desired). Details payload: `{via: 'list-with-stats', tenant, count, customer_ids: number[], page, per_page, include_stats}`. Only writes when `customers.length > 0` ŌĆö an empty result set isn't a PII access. (4) **Audit schema fit check** ŌĆö `audit_logs` (migration 022) only has columns `id, event, user_id, ip_address, details, created_at`. The task's suggested object shape (`entity_type`, `entity_id`, `tenant`) doesn't have matching columns, so `tenant`, `customer_id` / `customer_ids`, and `via` are packed into the existing `details` JSON instead ŌĆö preserves queryability (`json_extract(details, '$.customer_id') = ?`) without a schema migration, and the existing `audit(db, event, userId, ip, details)` signature already guards against details > 16KB and strips control chars from event strings. (5) **No write when user missing** ŌĆö `req.user?.id` defaults to `null` for unauthenticated surfaces (which shouldn't reach these handlers given middleware, but the audit row still records `user_id=NULL` + `ip` for insider-threat traceability of any auth middleware miss). (6) **Filter fingerprint fields chosen for equivalence, not exhaustiveness** ŌĆö `keyword`, `group_id`, `sort_by+sort_order`, `include_stats`, `from_date`, `to_date`, `has_open_tickets`, `offset`, `pageSize`. Changing any fires a new audit row; only an exact re-issue of the same query coalesces. Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ zero errors. Files: `packages/server/src/utils/customerViewAudit.ts` (new, 60 lines including comments), `packages/server/src/routes/customers.routes.ts` (+52/-2: new import, list-with-stats audit block before `res.json`, detail audit block after RFM / before `res.json`). Coalescing rationale: every list scan firing audit rows per-customer-per-page would turn a routine "open the customers page" interaction into 20-250 rows per click ŌĆö saturating `audit_logs`, pushing out more interesting events like failed logins and refunded deposits, and making retention policies painful. 5 minutes is short enough that an adversary cannot drain the directory in bursts without leaving at least one row per 5-min window, and long enough that ordinary UI interaction (pagination, sort toggles, refresh) stays quiet. (P3-PII-05)

- [x] PROD94. Added `CODE_OF_CONDUCT.md` at repo root using Contributor Covenant v2.1 text. - [x] SEC-H52. **Hash estimate `approval_token` at rest with SHA-256 + migration backfill.** Pre-fix: `POST /estimates/:id/send` generated `crypto.randomBytes(16).toString('hex')` and stored the raw plaintext in `estimates.approval_token`. Any DB dump (backup tar on a stale staff laptop, tenant export, operator error, or a full exfil) handed an attacker every unexpired, unused approval token for every pending estimate in the fleet ŌĆö they could mark each one approved via `POST /estimates/:id/approve` before the customer even opened the SMS, and because approval fires the SW-D7 auto-ticket-status hook, the blast radius leaked sideways into the tickets domain (estimates auto-converted ŌåÆ ticket status flipped on the shop floor without operator knowledge). Post-fix: (a) **Migration `107_estimate_approval_token_hash.sql`** adds `approval_token_hash TEXT` alongside the existing `approval_token TEXT` column plus a partial index `idx_estimates_approval_token_hash ON estimates(approval_token_hash) WHERE approval_token_hash IS NOT NULL`. Two-step rollover mirrors the SEC-H38 gift-card pattern in migration 104 ŌĆö legacy column stays during the grace window so in-flight send links don't break; a follow-up migration will drop it once the grace period closes. (b) **`services/estimateApprovalTokenHashBackfill.ts`** ŌĆö exports `hashEstimateApprovalToken(token)` (the canonical SHA-256 helper reused by the routes) and `backfillEstimateApprovalTokenHashes(db)`, an idempotent boot sweep that walks `estimates WHERE approval_token IS NOT NULL AND approval_token_hash IS NULL` and populates the hash column in a single transaction. Wired into `packages/server/src/index.ts` both for single-tenant (after seed) and per-tenant (inside `forEachDb` alongside the gift-card backfill). (c) **`/estimates/:id/send`** now generates `crypto.randomBytes(24).toString('base64url')` (24 bytes = 192 bits entropy, comfortably above the 128-bit guess bar) and issues `UPDATE estimates SET approval_token = NULL, approval_token_hash = ?, ŌĆ”` ŌĆö plaintext is explicitly nulled so even the one-shot write path leaves no plaintext at rest; the plaintext leaves the server exactly once in the response body, then gets delivered via SMS. (d) **`/estimates/:id/approve`** verify flow: hash the inbound token once, look up via `approval_token_hash` with `constantTimeEquals` (the existing `crypto.timingSafeEqual` wrapper). If the hash column is NULL on the row ŌĆö meaning the send happened before migration 107 and the backfill couldn't complete (or the row was written during the migration window) ŌĆö fall back once to the legacy plaintext column via `constantTimeEquals`, then run an in-place hash-migrate (`UPDATE estimates SET approval_token_hash = ?, approval_token = NULL WHERE id = ? AND approval_token_hash IS NULL`) so subsequent verifies take the hash-first path. The atomic consume-UPDATE was updated from `WHERE approval_token = ?` ŌåÆ `WHERE approval_token_hash = ?`, preserving the single-use + concurrent-approval race guards from SC4/S20-E2. (e) **Grace-path pattern**: hash-only at rest from migration 107 onward; legacy plaintext rows hash-migrate on first successful verify, draining the plaintext column naturally. No operator intervention required; no in-flight send links broken. (f) Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ zero errors. Files modified: `packages/server/src/db/migrations/107_estimate_approval_token_hash.sql` (new, 44 lines), `packages/server/src/services/estimateApprovalTokenHashBackfill.ts` (new, 80 lines), `packages/server/src/index.ts` (+29 / single-tenant + per-tenant backfill wiring), `packages/server/src/routes/estimates.routes.ts` (+60/-17: new import, hash-on-send, hash-first verify with legacy fallback, hash-based consume). (LOGIC-028)

- [x] SEC-H61. **Reset-password link `Referrer-Policy: no-referrer` + `history.replaceState` to strip token from URL.** Pre-fix: the reset-password URL `https://<tenant>.<baseDomain>/reset-password/<64-hex-token>` carried the single-use token as a path segment. If a user opened the link, then clicked any external asset that the browser would otherwise send a Referer header to (fonts.googleapis.com, any CDN link they happened to click, a screenshot posted to support chat, a screen share, or their browser-history export), the token leaked. The server already set `Referrer-Policy: strict-origin-when-cross-origin` globally via helmet (`packages/server/src/index.ts:833`) and explicitly `no-referrer` on two narrow surfaces (`/portal/api/v2` at line 1269 and `/api/v1/public/payment-links` at line 1366), but nothing hardened the web-app surface for this one page. Post-fix: (a) **`packages/web/index.html`** ŌĆö added `<meta name="referrer" content="no-referrer">` inside `<head>`, which forces every outbound request from any BizarreCRM page (including the reset-password page) to omit the Referer header entirely. Client-side belt-and-suspenders to the server header ŌĆö the stricter of the two always wins, so this doesn't regress any existing less-strict request (the meta tag is honored by every modern browser including WebView / Safari / Firefox / Chromium-based clients). (b) **`packages/web/src/pages/auth/ResetPasswordPage.tsx`** ŌĆö stashed the token in a `useRef` on mount (not `useState` ŌĆö keeps it out of React DevTools' state inspector and out of redux-devtools-like extensions that serialize hook state) and called `window.history.replaceState({}, '', '/reset-password')` inside a one-shot `useEffect(() => {...}, [])` so the token disappears from the address bar the instant the page renders. A screenshot, a screen share, a casual over-the-shoulder look, or a copy-paste of the URL into a support ticket no longer exfiltrates the token. Wrapped in a `try/catch` so very old browsers / sandboxed iframes that don't expose the history API fall through gracefully with the token still in the URL ŌĆö the form submission still works because we read from `tokenRef`, not from a fresh `useParams()` call. (c) **Token memory scrub on success** ŌĆö after `authApi.resetPassword(token, password)` resolves, we set `tokenRef.current = null`, `setPassword('')`, `setConfirmPassword('')` so the token AND the user's chosen password leave React's closure scope. The server invalidated the token server-side in the same request (single-use semantics: `UPDATE users SET ..., reset_token = NULL, reset_token_expires = NULL WHERE id = ?` at `auth.routes.ts:1485`), so even a replay of the stale value would fail ŌĆö but scrubbing prevents a later XSS / DOM inspection from reading the same string back out of memory between success and navigation. (d) **Backend already HTTPS-only** ŌĆö `packages/server/src/routes/auth.routes.ts:1400` emits `const resetUrl = \`https://${host}/reset-password/${resetToken}\`` unconditionally; no `http://` path exists. Confirmed by reading the forgot-password handler end-to-end. No change needed server-side. (e) **No external links in reset flow** ŌĆö `rel="noopener noreferrer"` sweep of `packages/web/src/pages/auth/` returned zero `target="_blank"` matches, so there's nothing to retrofit; the only links in `ResetPasswordPage.tsx` are internal React Router `<Link>` components to `/login` which don't render as `<a target>` and don't leak Referer by design. (f) **Existing SEC-H65 guards stay intact** ŌĆö the single-use token invalidation at auth.routes.ts:1483-1487 runs inside `adb.transaction([...])` so the "UPDATE users ... WHERE reset_token = ?" + DELETE-sessions pair commits atomically even under concurrent attempts; my change doesn't touch that transaction. (g) **Verified**: `cd packages/web && npm run build` built in 8.69s with zero TS errors, emitted SettingsPage / ResetPasswordPage / TicketDetailPage chunks identically to prior builds (only the ResetPasswordPage chunk changed). Files modified: `packages/web/index.html` (+5 lines including comment), `packages/web/src/pages/auth/ResetPasswordPage.tsx` (+35/-4, useRef + useEffect + success scrub). Commit 2053373.

- [x] SEC-H64. **Deposits apply + refund conditional UPDATE on `applied_to_invoice_id IS NULL AND refunded_at IS NULL`.** Pre-fix: `packages/server/src/routes/deposits.routes.ts` had two TOCTOU races. (a) `POST /:id/apply-to-invoice` (lines 180-230) read the deposit row, verified `applied_to_invoice_id IS NULL` and `refunded_at IS NULL` at the app layer, then issued an unconditional `UPDATE deposits SET applied_to_invoice_id=?, applied_at=? WHERE id=?`. Two concurrent POSTs (e.g. an impatient cashier double-tapping "Apply Deposit" on the touchscreen POS, or a legitimate apply racing a finalize-invoice flow that tries to apply the same deposit from a different code path) could both read `applied_to_invoice_id IS NULL`, both pass the if-guard, both run the UPDATE ŌĆö the second write silently clobbered the first, invoice balance math double-subtracted the deposit amount, and the audit log carried two conflicting `deposit.apply` events for what should have been one event. (b) `DELETE /:id` (lines 235-260) had the symmetric problem for refunds: pre-txn `SELECT` + app-layer `if (refunded_at) throw` + `if (applied_to_invoice_id) throw`, then unconditional `UPDATE deposits SET refunded_at=? WHERE id=?`. A concurrent apply+refund could both pass their respective checks and both commit; or two concurrent refund calls could both mark the row refunded with slightly different timestamps depending on which write landed last. Post-fix: moved the race safety from app layer to DB layer by pushing the `IS NULL` guards into the UPDATE's WHERE clause. (1) Apply handler now runs `UPDATE deposits SET applied_to_invoice_id=?, applied_at=? WHERE id=? AND applied_to_invoice_id IS NULL AND refunded_at IS NULL`, captures `updateResult.changes`, and throws `AppError 409 'Deposit already applied or refunded'` when `changes === 0`. (2) Refund handler runs `UPDATE deposits SET refunded_at=? WHERE id=? AND refunded_at IS NULL AND applied_to_invoice_id IS NULL` with the same 0-changes ŌåÆ 409 guard. SQLite's WAL mode serializes the writer at the page-lock level, so two concurrent UPDATEs with overlapping WHERE predicates are evaluated one at a time ŌĆö the loser sees the winner's mutation and its own WHERE clause no longer matches, `changes === 0`, 409 returned. The pre-check SELECT was retained in both handlers because it buys two things the atomic UPDATE alone cannot: (i) a clean `404 'Deposit not found'` for unknown ids instead of the ambiguous 409 an atomic UPDATE would emit, and (ii) access to `deposit.amount_cents` for the audit payload + response body (the UPDATE doesn't return the updated row in better-sqlite3's RunResult shape; we'd otherwise need a second SELECT after the UPDATE). Authorization gates (`requireManagerOrAdmin` on apply, `requireAdminDeposits` on refund) are untouched ŌĆö the race fix lives in the persistence layer, orthogonal to RBAC. Note: the task description suggested capturing `refund_reason` on refund but migration `095_billing_enrichment.sql` does not define a `refund_reason` column on `deposits` (columns are `id, ticket_id, customer_id, amount_cents, collected_at, applied_to_invoice_id, applied_at, refunded_at, notes`; migration 103 added `currency`). Introducing the column would require a new migration and isn't required to close the TOCTOU race, so it's out of scope for SEC-H64 ŌĆö the existing DELETE endpoint never accepted a reason and the new conditional UPDATE preserves that shape. Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ zero errors. Files modified: `packages/server/src/routes/deposits.routes.ts` (+29/-4, two conditional UPDATEs + audit comments). (C3-005, 006). The code change actually landed as part of commit `212c917` (sec-h63 stocktake) because the staged diff got bundled; functionally identical to what SEC-H64 required.

- [x] SEC-H63. **Transactional stocktake commit with `WHERE status='open'` guard inside txn.** Pre-fix: `POST /stocktake/:id/commit` at `packages/server/src/routes/stocktake.routes.ts:266-347` did a pre-txn `SELECT status` + `if (session.status !== 'open') throw`, then opened `db.transaction()` that (a) looped stocktake_counts updating `inventory_items.in_stock = ?` + inserting `stock_movements`, and (b) as the LAST txn statement flipped `stocktakes.status='committed'`. Two concurrent commit POSTs could both pass the pre-txn "is open" check (because the winner hadn't opened its txn yet), both enter their own transactions, both apply every variance ŌĆö double-adjusting every `in_stock` and double-writing `stock_movements` for every counted item. Partial failure after the stock writes would also have left the status='open' momentarily until the final UPDATE (minor ŌĆö the txn would roll it back anyway, but the ordering encoded no intent). Post-fix: moved the status flip to the FIRST mutation inside the single `db.transaction()` block and made it a conditional UPDATE: `UPDATE stocktakes SET status='committed', committed_at=datetime('now'), committed_by_user_id=? WHERE id=? AND status='open'`. Asserts `lockResult.changes === 1`; on `0`, sets `raceLost = true` and throws `AppError 409 'Stocktake is already being committed or was just closed'`. better-sqlite3's `transaction(fn)` wraps `BEGIN...COMMIT` and better-sqlite3 is synchronous ŌĆö so the `WHERE status='open'` predicate and the subsequent `UPDATE inventory_items` / `INSERT stock_movements` statements execute as an indivisible unit. A concurrent commit reaching its own txn sees the winner's already-committed `status='committed'`, its conditional UPDATE returns `changes=0`, the txn throws, rolls back, and returns 409. Because the status flip is INSIDE the txn, any mid-txn error (item went inactive, disk full, crash) rolls back everything ŌĆö including the status flip ŌĆö so the session returns to `status='open'` for a clean retry rather than being stuck in a half-committed state. The task description suggested a `'committing'` intermediate status, but migration 091 defines the schema `CHECK (status IN ('open', 'committed', 'cancelled'))` ŌĆö a third state would need a new migration. Folding the race guard directly into the `'open' ŌåÆ 'committed'` transition within the atomic txn achieves the same guarantee with less schema churn. Also added a `stocktake_commit_failed` audit event in the catch block with `{stocktake_id, race_lost, reason}` so race-loss AND any other mid-txn failure surface in `audit_log` ŌĆö previously only `stocktake_committed` (success) was audited, so a rolled-back commit left no forensic trail. Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ clean (zero errors). Files modified: `packages/server/src/routes/stocktake.routes.ts` (~40 net insertions, reordered one existing UPDATE). (BH-B-011). Commit 212c917.

- [x] PROD99. **Crash recovery: uncaught exceptions logged + process restarts ŌĆö verified.** Verification-only. Read `packages/server/src/index.ts:3081-3247`. Key evidence: (a) `handleFatal(type, error)` at line 3186 logs the fatal error via `log.error('FATAL: unrecoverable process error ŌĆö initiating shutdown', { type, route, errorName, errorMessage, stack })`, then calls `recordCrash()` (tracker), `emitCrashLog()` (JSON file at `packages/server/data/crash-log.json`), and `broadcast('management:crash', entry)` so any connected management dashboards see it immediately. (b) Installs a 10s force-exit timer via `setTimeout(() => process.exit(1), 10000)` so a wedged shutdown cannot leave a zombie. (c) Calls `shutdown(type)` which ŌĆö per line 3081 comment ŌĆö "exit with code 1 so PM2/systemd treats as a failed run worth restarting". (d) Both handlers wired: `process.on('uncaughtException', ...)` at line 3240, `process.on('unhandledRejection', ...)` at line 3244. Neither path ever silently swallows ŌĆö every branch either logs before exit or fires `recordCrash()` before exit. `ecosystem.config.js` at repo root configures PM2 to restart on non-zero exit.

- [x] PROD101. **`/readyz` checks DB connectivity ŌĆö verified.** Verification-only. The endpoint is named `/api/v1/health/ready`, not `/readyz` ŌĆö naming delta only, functionality matches acceptance criteria. Read `packages/server/src/index.ts:1502-1531`: (a) returns `503 {success:false,message:'Server is still starting'}` while the global `isReady` boot flag is false (set to true only after `migrateAllTenants()` resolves, per comment at line 1497-1501). (b) Once ready, runs a second DB round-trip via `db.prepare('PRAGMA user_version').get()` to catch post-boot DB degradation (file pulled out, schema migration in flight, WAL corruption). On prepare/get failure, returns `503 {success:false,message:'db unreachable'}` so orchestrators drain traffic instead of sending requests that will 500. (c) On success, returns 200 with `{status:'ready', degraded: readyError !== null, schemaVersion: userVersion}` ŌĆö the `degraded` flag flips to true when per-tenant migrations had partial failures but core is usable, giving orchestrators a three-way signal (healthy / degraded / unreachable). Suitable for K8s readiness probe / LB activation-gate configuration.

- [x] PROD116. **Migration prefix collision handled safely ŌĆö verified.** Verification-only. Read `packages/server/src/db/migrate.ts` end-to-end (81 lines). (a) The `_migrations` tracking table at line 10-16 defines `name TEXT NOT NULL UNIQUE` ŌĆö full filename is the PK, not just the numeric prefix, so `049_customer_is_active.sql` + `049_po_status_workflow.sql` + `049_sms_scheduled_and_archival.sql` each get their own row. (b) `readdirSync(migrationsDir).filter(f => f.endsWith('.sql')).sort()` at line 24-26 ŌĆö JS `Array.prototype.sort()` with no comparator defaults to UTF-16 lexicographic, which is deterministic across the three 049 files (`c < p < s` on the char-17 position) and the two 050 files (`a < l`). Rerun on any OS: identical order. (c) Per-migration execution at line 32-63 reads the full filename's applied-status against the `applied` Set built from `_migrations.name`, so a missing migration re-runs while applied ones skip. (d) INSERT INTO _migrations at line 53 / 60 uses the full filename; a duplicate INSERT would throw on the UNIQUE constraint and fail the migration transaction loudly ŌĆö no silent skip path. (e) Migration fail handler at line 65-69 rethrows with a descriptive message ŌĆö zero swallow. Conclusion: collisions are cosmetic filename artifacts; migrate.ts handles them correctly.

- [x] PROD59. **Self-service tenant termination ŌĆö multi-step-confirm endpoint + 30-day soft-delete grace window + daily purge cron + Settings > Danger Zone UI.** Pre-fix: there was no tenant-facing path to terminate an account. The super-admin `/super-admin/api/tenants/:slug` DELETE soft-deleted via `deleteTenant()` (which already respects a 30-day grace via `archive/`) but required a platform super-admin ŌĆö a tenant who wanted out had to email support. Per the project memory rule "tenant DB files are sacred ŌĆö this is the ONE allowed deletion path: explicit, user-initiated," PROD59 wires up that one allowed path with maximum friction so nothing short of a fully-intentional admin action can cross the line. Post-fix: new `packages/server/src/services/tenantTermination.ts` (~360 lines) owns the three-stage state machine and the filesystem operation. Tokens live in an in-memory `Map` with a 5-minute TTL + `setInterval` reaper. Token equality uses `crypto.timingSafeEqual` on UTF-8 buffers so the slug/phrase comparisons don't leak length via timing. (a) **`POST /api/v1/admin/terminate-tenant`** mounted inside `packages/server/src/routes/admin.routes.ts` BEFORE the token-based admin-panel auth middleware AND before the multi-tenant kill-switch ŌĆö uses the tenant JWT via `authMiddleware` + `req.user.role === 'admin'` gate, so it's reachable from a shop's own Settings even though the rest of `/api/v1/admin/*` is super-admin-only. Three branches on `action`: (b) **`action: 'request'`** ŌĆö mints a fresh 32-byte hex token via `crypto.randomBytes(32).toString('hex')`, stores `{ slug, tenantId, adminUserId, adminUsername, adminEmail, stage: 'issued', expiresAt }` in the in-memory Map, sends a best-effort notification email to the tenant's `admin_email` (via the existing per-tenant `sendEmail(db, opts)` which reads SMTP config from `store_config`; failure does NOT block token return ŌĆö if SMTP is misconfigured the caller who just authenticated still gets the token), and returns `{ token, expires_at }`. Email body explains what happened, shows the requesting IP + admin username + expiry, tells the recipient that IF they didn't initiate this they can ignore it (token auto-expires), and nudges them to rotate their password via the linked app URL. Single-tenant mode returns 400 with a clear error telling operators to remove their self-hosted install manually. (c) **`action: 'confirm'`** ŌĆö caller posts `{ token, typed_slug }`, server validates the token still exists + hasn't expired + has stage `'issued'`, and `timingSafeEquals` the typed slug against the stored slug (case-sensitive). On match the token's stage advances to `'slug_confirmed'` and we return `{ stage: 'slug_confirmed' }`. Mismatch returns 400 with a generic "Typed subdomain does not match" message so attackers can't probe for existing token/slug pairs. (d) **`action: 'finalize'`** ŌĆö the only branch that actually touches state. Requires (i) a valid unexpired token in stage `'slug_confirmed'`, (ii) the slug typed correctly AGAIN (defense-in-depth against token theft between step 2 and step 3), and (iii) the literal string `"DELETE ALL DATA PERMANENTLY"` as `typed_phrase`. Whitespace-sensitive, case-sensitive, no punctuation. If all three match, the token is deleted from the Map FIRST (so a retry of the same POST on client timeout cannot double-execute), then `executeTermination()` performs the soft-delete. (e) **Soft-delete pipeline**: `closeTenantDb(slug)` drops the live DB handle so Windows can rename the file; `fs.renameSync(tenantDataDir/<slug>.db, tenantDataDir/deleted/<slug>-<iso-ts>.db)` (plus WAL + SHM sidecars, best-effort); master DB `tenants` row flips to `status = 'pending_deletion'` with `deletion_scheduled_at` set to now + 30 days and `archived_db_path` set to the new location for operator visibility; a `tenant_self_terminated` row goes into `master_audit_log` with the archived path + scheduled times; Cloudflare DNS record deletion is best-effort (failure is logged but does NOT abort the flow ŌĆö user's intent is already expressed and a dangling DNS record is a lesser evil than leaving the DB live); session invalidation is implicit ŌĆö the `sessions` table lives inside the just-renamed file, so any outstanding access token for this tenant hits authMiddleware's session-lookup on the NEXT request and gets rejected cleanly (no server-side logout loop needed). (f) **Response shape**: `{ success: true, deletion_scheduled_at, permanent_delete_at, grace_days: 30 }` so the client has a paper trail to show the user (and save for their records). (g) **Audit log every step**: `tenant_terminate_step1_request`, `tenant_terminate_step2_confirm` (with `matched: true|false`), `tenant_terminate_step3_finalize_attempt`, `tenant_terminate_step3_finalize_rejected` (with reason), `tenant_terminate_finalized`, plus `tenant_terminate_refused_single_tenant` for single-tenant-mode refusals. Every event goes through the existing `audit(db, event, userId, ip, details)` helper in `utils/audit.ts` so AuditLogsTab picks them up automatically. (h) **Daily purge cron** in `packages/server/src/index.ts` under the existing `trackInterval(...)` block (multi-tenant mode only, lazy-imports `purgeExpiredDeletions` from the service): every hour the cron checks if the current UTC hour is 03, and if `shouldRunDaily('tenant-termination-purge', 'UTC')` returns true, calls `purgeExpiredDeletions()`. The sweeper walks `deleted/` and unlinks any `*.db`/`*.db-wal`/`*.db-shm` whose `mtime` is older than `TERMINATION_GRACE_DAYS` (30). We also kick one purge at startup so a server that was offline through a scheduled deletion catches up on boot ŌĆö the "never delete earlier than scheduled" invariant holds because the cutoff is mtime-based, not tick-based. (i) **Front-end UI** ŌĆö new `packages/web/src/pages/settings/DangerZoneTab.tsx` (4-step modal state machine: `intro ŌåÆ request ŌåÆ confirm_slug ŌåÆ confirm_phrase ŌåÆ done`, with a "Request Account Termination" button on the landing tab that's disabled unless `useAuthStore().user.role === 'admin'`). Each step has a dedicated sub-component. Step 4 renders the `deletion_scheduled_at` + `permanent_delete_at` timestamps from the server response so the user has a visible grace-window countdown. Wiring: `SettingsPage.tsx` got a new `'danger-zone'` tab in the Tab union, a tabs-array entry with the `AlertTriangle` icon, a TAB_KEYWORDS row for search, and a conditional `{activeTab === 'danger-zone' && <DangerZoneTab />}` in the render. `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` gained `tenantTerminationApi = { request(), confirm(token, slug), finalize(token, slug, phrase) }` with typed response shapes. (j) **Verified**: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌĆö zero errors. `cd packages/web && npm run build` ŌĆö built in 8.77s, SettingsPage chunk 362.75kB (gzip 69.84kB). Files added: `packages/server/src/services/tenantTermination.ts` (~360 lines), `packages/web/src/pages/settings/DangerZoneTab.tsx` (~400 lines). Files modified: `packages/server/src/routes/admin.routes.ts` (~110 lines: endpoint handler + bypass for existing middleware), `packages/server/src/index.ts` (+40 lines: daily purge cron), `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` (+30 lines: typed API), `packages/web/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` (+10 lines: tab wiring), `TODO.md` (migrated). Commit e0fa615.

- [x] PROD58. **Per-tenant "download all my data" capability ŌĆö GDPR/CCPA JSON export endpoint + Settings UI button.** Pre-fix: there was no tenant-facing way to obtain a full data archive. The existing `/api/v1/settings-ext/export.json` only covered `store_config` (shop settings); the `/api/v1/admin/backup` path produces encrypted backups that require the server's key to read and is disabled in multi-tenant mode. GDPR Article 20 (right to data portability) and CCPA Section 1798.110 (right to know) both require the data subject to receive a copy of their personal data in a machine-readable format on request ŌĆö neither of the existing endpoints satisfied that for a tenant admin. Post-fix: new `packages/server/src/routes/dataExport.routes.ts` (~300 lines) mounted at `/api/v1/data-export` via `authMiddleware` so it inherits the tenant resolver's `req.db` assignment (tenant DB in multi-tenant, global DB in single-tenant). (a) **`GET /export-all-data`** ŌĆö admin-role-gated (`adminOnly` middleware inside the router throws 403 if `req.user?.role !== 'admin'`). Reads `last_data_export_at` from `store_config` as a per-tenant rate-limit checkpoint ŌĆö if another export fired in the last hour the endpoint returns 429 with `Retry-After` header + a `retry_after_seconds` payload so the UI can render a countdown. On success, writes a fresh ISO timestamp to `store_config.last_data_export_at` BEFORE streaming begins (a client that intentionally disconnects early still spends the slot ŌĆö protects against abuse loops). Lists every user-owned table via `SELECT name FROM sqlite_master WHERE type = 'table' AND name NOT LIKE 'sqlite_%'`, then streams the JSON envelope `{"tenant_slug":"...","exported_at":"...","version":1,"tables":{"customers":[...],"tickets":[...],...},"row_counts":{...}}` one row at a time via `res.write(JSON.stringify(row))`. Writing per-row instead of per-table keeps peak process memory bounded for large tenants (a 500k-row invoices table no longer balloons the heap before the first byte hits the wire). (b) **Sensitive-field redaction** ŌĆö the `users` table's `password_hash / totp_secret / pin_hash / recovery_codes / reset_token_hash / remember_token_hash` columns are rewritten to `null` before emission via `sanitizeRow(table, row)`, and `store_config` rows whose `key` matches `SENSITIVE_CONFIG_KEYS` (BlockChyp keys, SMS provider tokens, `smtp_pass`, `tcx_password`, `stripe_secret_key`, `twilio_auth_token`) have their `value` nulled ŌĆö the export is for the tenant's own GDPR/CCPA records, not for onward transmission, and handing a plaintext bearer token to whoever intercepts the JSON file on its way to the user's disk is a gift an attacker should not receive. `EXCLUDED_TABLES` drops bookkeeping tables entirely (`_migrations`, `sqlite_sequence`, `sessions`, `refresh_tokens`, `password_history`, `login_attempts`, `rate_limits`, `rate_limit_windows`, `api_key_revocations`, `admin_tokens`, `pending_2fa_challenges`, `recovery_codes_used`) because they hold short-lived auth state with no portability value. (c) **Audit log entry** ŌĆö always fires at end of request (even if the stream aborted mid-flight) via `audit(db, 'data_export', userId, ip, { tenant, filename, table_count, row_counts, total_rows })`. The `data_export` event joins the existing audit-log surface so AuditLogsTab can render it. (d) **Filename** ŌĆö `bizarre-crm-export-<slug>-<YYYY-MM-DD>.json`, slug-sanitized via `safeFilenameToken` (anything outside `[a-z0-9-_]` collapses to `-`, capped at 64 chars) so an exotic tenant slug cannot inject header-breaking characters. `Content-Disposition: attachment`, `Content-Type: application/json; charset=utf-8`, `Cache-Control: no-store`, `Pragma: no-cache`, `X-Robots-Tag: noindex, nofollow`. (e) **`GET /export-all-data/status`** ŌĆö read-only sibling endpoint returning `{ last_export_at, next_allowed_in_seconds, allowed, rate_limit_window_seconds }` so the Settings UI can render the "last exported" timestamp + "next allowed in N min" countdown without having to try the real endpoint and catch a 429. (f) **Web UI** ŌĆö `packages/web/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx`: added `DownloadAllDataSection` component at the top of the Data & Import tab (above the Factory Wipe red-border card, below the import-progress panel). Primary-orange `<Download />` button with copy "Download all my data" + subtitle explaining GDPR/CCPA scope + what secrets are stripped + the one-per-hour limit. `useQuery` polls `/data-export/export-all-data/status` every 60s so the enabled/disabled state auto-updates without reload. `useCallback`-wrapped `triggerDownload()` calls `dataExportApi.downloadAll()` with `responseType: 'blob'`, parses `Content-Disposition` to pull the server-suggested filename, materializes the Blob via `URL.createObjectURL`, clicks a hidden `<a>` to trigger the browser's save dialog, then revokes the URL. `confirm()` dialog before the download so an accidental click doesn't start a multi-megabyte archive. 429 responses come back as Blobs (because of `responseType: 'blob'`) so the error path reads the Blob back via `.text()` + `JSON.parse()` to surface the server's `message` in a toast, then re-fetches status so the countdown reflects the block. (g) **Typed client** ŌĆö `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` gained `dataExportApi = { status(), downloadAll() }` with a named `DataExportStatus` interface so downstream callers get autocomplete on the four response fields. Verified: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌåÆ zero errors; `cd packages/web && npm run build` ŌåÆ built in 8.64s, SettingsPage chunk 350.56kB (gzip 67.33kB). Files added: `packages/server/src/routes/dataExport.routes.ts` (312 lines). Files modified: `packages/server/src/index.ts` (+8 lines: import + mount), `packages/web/src/api/endpoints.ts` (+25 lines: typed api surface), `packages/web/src/pages/settings/SettingsPage.tsx` (+118 lines: DownloadAllDataSection component + usage + import), `TODO.md` (PROD58 migrated). - [x] PROD78-79-80-81. **Public-release docs: MIT LICENSE + public README + LICENSES.md + workspace-root pointer.** Phase-10 repo-polish cluster landed as one change because the four items share a single audience (anyone cloning the repo from GitHub for the first time) and cross-reference each other (README links LICENSE + LICENSES.md; LICENSES.md notes LICENSE covers the project itself; workspace-root pointer README defers to the repo README). (a) **PROD80 ŌĆö LICENSE (MIT)**: new `LICENSE` file at `bizarre-crm/` repo root, canonical MIT text, copyright line `Copyright (c) 2026 Bizarre Electronics CRM contributors`. MIT chosen over Apache-2.0 / AGPL / proprietary because: (1) repair-shop tooling has no patent-sensitivity justifying Apache-2.0's extra clauses for a solo-maintainer project, (2) AGPL's network-clause would poison any prospective managed-hosting partner who wants to run the server for a shop without being forced to redistribute their ops scripts, (3) MIT is the broadest-compatibility permissive license ŌĆö every third-party dep in `LICENSES.md` (MIT, ISC, Apache-2.0, BSD) is already upstream-compatible with MIT downstream, and forking shops can drop the project into whatever downstream arrangement they need without a compatibility audit.
