- [x] SA1-1. **JWT secrets can now be rotated gracefully without invalidating every active session.** Pre-fix: every `jwt.verify(token, config.jwtSecret, ...)` and `jwt.verify(refreshToken, config.jwtRefreshSecret, ...)` used a single secret. Rotating `JWT_SECRET` meant every already-issued access + refresh token failed verification the instant the server restarted, kicking every logged-in user out of the app mid-workday. Operators therefore avoided rotating JWT secrets even when they had reason to (suspected leak, routine credential hygiene, staff offboarding with deploy-shell access) ŌĆö the user-facing churn of forcing every employee to re-authenticate was worse than the perceived risk. Post-fix: new `utils/jwtSecrets.ts` module exposes `verifyJwtWithRotation(token, 'access'|'refresh', options)` which tries the current secret first and falls back to the optional `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` / `JWT_REFRESH_SECRET_PREVIOUS` secret ONLY on signature-verification failure (`JsonWebTokenError` whose `.name === 'JsonWebTokenError'`). TokenExpiredError / NotBeforeError are NOT rescued by the fallback ŌĆö expired tokens should stay expired regardless of which key signed them. Signing always uses the current secret; the previous secret is verify-only so leaving it set forever by accident cannot produce new tokens signed with it. (a) **`config.ts`** ŌĆö added `jwtSecretPrevious` + `jwtRefreshSecretPrevious` IIFE accessors that read `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` / `JWT_REFRESH_SECRET_PREVIOUS` from env, return `undefined` when unset, and refuse to load obviously-insecure placeholders (the well-known `change-me-*` / `dev-*-change-me` strings, plus any value shorter than 32 chars) with a warning so an operator who accidentally pastes a dev value into the previous slot doesn't silently widen the verification surface. (b) **`middleware/auth.ts`** ŌĆö `authMiddleware`'s `jwt.verify(token, config.jwtSecret, ...)` now routes through `verifyJwtWithRotation(token, 'access', ...)`. Import of `jwt` was kept for `JsonWebTokenError`-shape checks elsewhere in the file but `jwt.verify` no longer appears here. (c) **`ws/server.ts`** ŌĆö websocket auth uses the same rotation-aware verifier so a token that passes HTTP auth also passes WS auth (symmetric behavior is required ŌĆö otherwise a rotation would silently break realtime updates). `config` import became unused after the refactor and was removed. (d) **`routes/auth.routes.ts`** ŌĆö the `POST /refresh` handler's refresh-token verify uses `verifyJwtWithRotation(refreshToken, 'refresh', ...)`. Access-token signing + refresh-token signing both untouched: they always use the current secret. (e) **`routes/super-admin.routes.ts`** ŌĆö new `POST /rotate-jwt-secret` endpoint gated by the existing `superAdminAuth` middleware. Accepts `{ purpose: 'access' | 'refresh' | 'both' }` (default `'both'`), generates fresh 64-byte hex secret(s) via `generateJwtSecret()`, returns them in the response body along with a step-by-step instructions array. Deliberately does NOT write to process.env ŌĆö Node env mutations don't propagate to child workers, and in real deploys the env is owned by systemd / PM2 / Docker / Kubernetes secrets / a vault. The endpoint records `super_admin_rotate_jwt_secret` in `master_audit_log` with the purpose + a sanity-check hex-char count but never the secret value itself. (f) **`utils/startupValidation.ts`** ŌĆö calls new `warnIfPreviousSecretsSet()` helper which emits a 5-line boot warning whenever either `_PREVIOUS` env is still set, pointing to `docs/operator-guide.md` for the removal procedure. This nag fires on every restart until operators remove the vars, so stale rotation state is visible. (g) **`.env.example`** ŌĆö documents `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` + `JWT_REFRESH_SECRET_PREVIOUS` with the rotation workflow in a comment. (h) **`docs/operator-guide.md`** ŌĆö new "JWT Secret Rotation" section before "Backups": 5-step graceful procedure (generate ŌåÆ move old to _PREVIOUS ŌåÆ restart ŌåÆ wait ~90 min ŌåÆ remove _PREVIOUS ŌåÆ restart), explanation of why sign always uses current while verify accepts both, pointer to the super-admin rotation endpoint for multi-tenant setups, and note that the app never writes to env itself. (i) **`scripts/test-jwt-rotation.mjs`** ŌĆö 6 unit tests covering the critical paths: current-secret token verifies, previous-secret token verifies during rotation window, nonsense-secret token fails, rotation is opt-in (no previous = old tokens reject), expired tokens throw `TokenExpiredError` not rescued by fallback, and new tokens are always signed HS256 regardless of rotation state. Reconstructs the verifier in plain JS so the test is hermetic and doesn't drag in `config.ts`'s `process.exit` side-effects. Verified with `cd packages/server && node scripts/test-jwt-rotation.mjs` ŌåÆ **6 passed, 0 failed**. TypeScript clean: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌĆö no errors. Behavioural diff for operators who DON'T rotate: exactly zero ŌĆö `JWT_SECRET_PREVIOUS` defaults to undefined, the fallback branch is never taken, and every verify goes through `jwt.verify(token, config.jwtSecret, options)` via a one-line wrapper. Commit aa65ce5.

- [x] SA7-1. **Blocking sleep loops now have persistent per-job checkpoints so a mid-import crash can resume instead of replaying the whole queue.** Pre-fix: `packages/server/src/scripts/reimport-notes.ts` and `packages/server/src/services/repairDeskImport.ts#importTicketNotesAndHistory` walked the `import_id_map` for every imported RepairDesk ticket with a per-record `await sleep(200)` between fetches; `packages/server/src/services/myRepairAppImport.ts` and `packages/server/src/services/repairShoprImport.ts` did the same at page granularity. The loop cursor was a stack-local `processed` counter ŌĆö a Node crash, OOM kill, or operator Ctrl-C lost it entirely and the only recovery path was "rerun from 0", which replays thousands of external API requests and risks double-writes against the remote catalog. Post-fix: new migration `106_import_job_state.sql` adds the `import_job_state(job_id TEXT PK, step INT, total INT, last_processed_id TEXT, status, last_error, started_at, updated_at)` table with indexes on `status` and `updated_at`. New helper module `packages/server/src/services/importJobState.ts` exposes `buildJobId(source, entity, tenantSlug)` for a stable key format, `resumeJobState(db, jobId, { total, startFresh })` to claim/create the row, `parseResumeFlags(argv)` for shared CLI parsing, plus a handle object with `shouldSkip(recordId, rowIndex) / checkpoint({ step, lastProcessedId }) / markRunning / markPaused / complete / fail`. The critical invariant: `checkpoint()` is called from INSIDE the same `db.transaction(() => { ... })` that performs the row writes, so progress and writes commit or roll back together ŌĆö a crash mid-batch never leaves the cursor ahead of the data (or vice versa). `shouldSkip()` supports both cursor-based (source id) and index-based (row position) comparison; numeric ids use `<=` ordering so a resume after ticket N skips everything N and earlier. Patched call sites: (a) **`scripts/reimport-notes.ts`** ŌĆö added `import { buildJobId, resumeJobState, parseResumeFlags, type ResumeCliFlags }`, extended `CliArgs` with `ResumeCliFlags`, rewrote the argv parser to also accept `--resume` / `--start-fresh` (mutually exclusive; default is start-fresh to preserve "re-run from 0" muscle memory). The main loop now iterates by index so `shouldSkip(rdId, idx)` can short-circuit. Each ticket's notes + history INSERTs + `jobState.checkpoint({ step, lastProcessedId: rdId })` all live inside one `db.transaction(() => { ... })()`. Skip paths (already-has-notes, non-429 HTTP error, `json.success === false`) still checkpoint so a resume doesn't revisit them; 429 rate-limit and network errors intentionally DON'T checkpoint so the same ticket is retried on restart. Fatal errors in the outer main() catch call `jobState.fail(msg)` best-effort. (b) **`services/repairDeskImport.ts#importTicketNotesAndHistory`** ŌĆö same pattern for the in-process import path: takes an optional `{ startFresh }` opt (defaults to false for in-process continuity), builds `buildJobId('repairdesk', 'ticket-notes-history', tenantSlug)`, checkpoints inside the notes+history transaction, respects cancelFlags via `jobState.markPaused()`, and advances `jobState.complete(processed)` on clean exit. `cancelFlags` (existing tenant-scoped Ctrl-C signal) now properly marks the row paused instead of leaving it in 'running' forever. (c) **`scripts/full-import.ts`** ŌĆö usage docs updated to mention the forwarded `--resume` / `--start-fresh` flags; no code change needed because it already spawns reimport-notes via `await import('./reimport-notes.js')` which inherits process.argv. Shared CLI parser: `parseResumeFlags(argv)` throws if both flags are passed, defaults to `startFresh: true` if neither (conservative ŌĆö matches original behavior), and lives in importJobState.ts so future import scripts pick it up for free. Out of scope for this patch (no data-write loops to checkpoint ŌĆö these are page-fetch-only loops that feed the *already-transactional* entity-import batches, which have their own `import_id_map` idempotence via `findMapping` lookups): the top-level page loops in `RdApiClient.fetchAllPages` / `RsApiClient.fetchAllPages` / `MraApiClient.fetchInventoryPages`. Those already resume correctly because `insertMapping.run(runId, entity, rdId, localId)` is called inside the per-batch transaction and `findMapping` skips records that already have a row ŌĆö the import_id_map itself IS their checkpoint. Adding a second checkpoint for them would be redundant and would serialize extra UPDATEs against a hot table. Verified with `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌĆö exit code 0, zero errors. Migration file: `packages/server/src/db/migrations/106_import_job_state.sql` (55 lines, two indexes). Files added: `services/importJobState.ts` (248 lines). Files modified: `scripts/reimport-notes.ts` (~60 lines diff), `scripts/full-import.ts` (docstring-only), `services/repairDeskImport.ts` (~50 lines diff in `importTicketNotesAndHistory`). Commit 1f50f6e.

- [x] SA10-1. **Lingering `as any` casts at the webhook / invoice event-broadcast boundary removed ŌĆö three call sites now use narrowed types.** Pre-fix: `packages/server/src/routes/invoices.routes.ts:318` (`fireWebhook(db, 'invoice_created', { invoice_id, order_id: (invoice as any)?.order_id })`) and `packages/server/src/routes/tickets.routes.ts:1149` + `:2095` carried `(<row> as any)?.order_id` escape-hatch casts. Root cause: `getInvoiceDetail` / `getFullTicketAsync` spread `adb.get<any>(...)` rows into their return value, so the detail-row types were loose `any`/`AnyRow = Record<string, any>` shapes that Typescript couldn't verify; the cast at the broadcast boundary silenced the "possibly undefined" lint without actually answering the question "does this row really have an `order_id` string?". Post-fix: (a) `invoices.routes.ts` ŌĆö the POST `/invoices` handler ALREADY computed the invoice `orderId` locally earlier in the handler (`const orderId = formatInvoiceOrderId(nextSeq)` at line 226), and that's the literal value we INSERT into `invoices.order_id`. The webhook fire-site now uses that local variable directly ŌĆö same value, zero cast. (b) `tickets.routes.ts:1149` ŌĆö symmetric fix; the POST handler has `const orderId = formatTicketOrderId(ticketSeq)` in scope at line 972 (well before the line-1149 webhook fire-site), so the `ticket_created` webhook now passes `orderId` directly instead of reading it back off `ticket` via a cast. (c) `tickets.routes.ts:2095` ŌĆö the PATCH `/tickets/:id/status` handler does NOT have a local `orderId` available (it receives the ticket id on the URL and only fetches the full ticket via `getFullTicketAsync` afterward). Replaced the `(ticket as any)?.order_id` with a typed-narrowing pattern: `const ticketOrderId = ticket && typeof (ticket as { order_id?: unknown }).order_id === 'string' ? (ticket as { order_id: string }).order_id : undefined`. The `{ order_id?: unknown }` shape lets us ask the question, `typeof === 'string'` actually answers it, and the narrowed `{ order_id: string }` accessor is safe because the guard just proved the shape. Preserves the identical null/undefined fallback semantics the original optional-chain produced (if `ticket` is null, or `order_id` is missing / non-string, the webhook body receives `undefined` ŌĆö exactly what the old `(ticket as any)?.order_id` would have yielded). Behavioural diff: zero. Every webhook payload is byte-for-byte identical to before; only the type-checker's view of the code changed. Verified with `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌĆö exit code 0, zero errors. Files touched: `routes/invoices.routes.ts` (+5/-1), `routes/tickets.routes.ts` (+12/-2). Commit 6f0b376.

- [x] SA8-1. **Deep link validation ŌĆö verified non-applicable after a full cross-package sweep.** The audit finding asserted that "the Electron app now implements a per-user installation without UAC, but the `setup` URL handlers lack strict deep-link origin validation, allowing potential arbitrary custom protocol abuse." After grepping `packages/management/` and the packaged `dashboard/` output for every Electron API that can surface a custom-scheme URL to the main process ŌĆö `app.setAsDefaultProtocolClient`, `protocol.register*`, `protocol.handle`, `registerSchemesAsPrivileged`, `app.on('open-url', ŌĆ”)` (macOS), `app.on('second-instance', ŌĆ”)` (Windows/Linux), `app.requestSingleInstanceLock()`, and `process.argv` parsing for a custom scheme ŌĆö the result is zero occurrences in source. The management app is NOT registered as a custom URL-scheme handler with the OS, does not take a single-instance lock, has no `open-url` / `second-instance` listener, and performs no `process.argv` scanning for `bizarrecrm://`-style URIs. The audit's phrase "`setup` URL handlers" appears to conflate the `management:setup` IPC channel (the initial admin-user bootstrap flow in `packages/management/src/main/ipc/management-api.ts:254`, which accepts `username` + `password` arguments and POSTs to `/api/v1/management/setup` ŌĆö no URL involved) with a custom deep-link route that does not exist. The only URL parsing performed by the main process is **outbound-gating**: `isAllowedRendererUrl()` in `packages/management/src/main/window.ts:42-58` (allows only `file://` + the Vite dev-server origin for in-place navigation via `will-navigate`), the `setWindowOpenHandler` block at `window.ts:130-142` (passes window-open targets to `shell.openExternal` only when `protocol === 'http:' | 'https:'`), and `isSafeLocalUrl()` in `packages/management/src/main/ipc/system-info.ts:23-35` (gates `system:open-external` to loopback `http(s)` hosts only). All three are defensive checks that reject foreign/hostile URLs the renderer might hand *out* to the OS ŌĆö the opposite threat direction from the one SA8-1 describes. The Android app and the iOS app DO register `bizarrecrm://` schemes (`packages/android/app/src/main/AndroidManifest.xml:68`, `ios/App/DeepLinkRouter.swift:23`, `ios/scripts/write-info-plist.sh:132`), and both already gate handoff with scheme-equality checks + route whitelists (`MainActivity.kt:196` `data.scheme != "bizarrecrm"` + `resolveDeepLink()` whitelist at `MainActivity.kt:259`; `DeepLinkRouter.swift:23` scheme guard) ŌĆö those are covered by AND-20260414-H1/H2 and the iOS-side `DeepLinkRouter` enum allow-list, not by SA8-1 which is scoped to the Electron desktop app. Closing with no code change. If a future release adds a `bizarrecrm-management://` protocol client, the implementation must register via `app.setAsDefaultProtocolClient`, take a single-instance lock, parse the deep-link via `new URL(raw)` (never `raw.startsWith`), enforce `protocol === 'bizarrecrm-management:'` exactly, whitelist the `hostname` against a closed set of verbs (e.g. `login-token`, `open-ticket`), reject any URL with embedded credentials (`parsed.username || parsed.password`) or non-ASCII/control-char query values, cap total URL length at 2048 chars, and reject unrecognized verbs with a `console.warn` + renderer toast rather than silently falling through. That checklist is recorded here as the spec for whoever opens that door; until then there is nothing to patch and no unit test to write (the deep-link path does not exist in the management package, and scaffolding a test harness purely to cover an absent feature would be noise). Verified via repeat `grep -ri 'setAsDefaultProtocolClient|open-url|second-instance|requestSingleInstanceLock' packages/management/ dashboard/` ŌĆö 0 hits in source; only prose mentions of `bizarrecrm://` appear in `docs/howtoIOS.md`, `ios/App/*.swift`, and `packages/android/**`, none of which live in the Electron app.

- [x] AUD-20260414-H3. **`/pos/checkout-with-ticket` now executes all ticket/invoice/payment writes as one atomic transaction ŌĆö partial-failure orphan rows eliminated.** Pre-fix: the route ran ~15 independent `await adb.run(...)` calls for the full checkout sequence (tickets INSERT ŌåÆ ticket_devices INSERTs ŌåÆ ticket_device_parts INSERTs ŌåÆ ticket totals UPDATE ŌåÆ ticket_history INSERT ŌåÆ invoice INSERT/UPDATE ŌåÆ invoice_line_items DELETE+INSERT ŌåÆ tickets.invoice_id UPDATE ŌåÆ payments INSERTs ŌåÆ pos_transactions INSERT ŌåÆ store_credits UPDATE/INSERT ŌåÆ store_credit_transactions INSERT ŌåÆ inventory_items stock-decrement UPDATE ŌåÆ stock_movements INSERT ŌåÆ tickets.status_id close UPDATE ŌåÆ ticket_history status_change INSERT). An existing batched `paymentTxQueries` block only covered steps 5e onward; everything before it wrote independently. Any mid-sequence failure ŌĆö a stock race triggering 409, a status lookup returning null, a connection drop, a FK violation ŌĆö left orphan tickets, $0 invoices, zero-line invoices, or payments pointing at half-closed tickets that required manual reconciliation. The route's own inline comment at `pos.routes.ts:1508-1511` explicitly acknowledged the gap: "A full atomic wrapping transaction for this endpoint is out of scope". Post-fix: split the handler into preflight + atomic-write + post-commit phases. **Preflight phase (async reads, no writes)**: resolves customer + tax class + membership + referral config + warranty defaults (consolidated from 2*N SELECTs per device into one SELECT for the default row), builds a `PreparedDevice[]` / `PreparedPart[]` / `PreparedProductLine[]` plan with every write parameter pre-computed, allocates `ticketOrderId` + `invoiceOrderId` upfront via `allocateCounter` so subqueries can resolve FKs during the batch, looks up `closedStatusId` + existing store_credits row + existing invoice ŌĆö ALL reads live here. **Atomic-write phase**: every INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE gets pushed into a single `TxQuery[]` and fired through `adb.transaction(txQueries)` in one call. Cross-table FKs inside the batch use order_id as a natural key (`(SELECT id FROM tickets WHERE order_id = ?)`, `(SELECT id FROM invoices WHERE order_id = ?)`) to avoid threading row-ids through async boundaries; parts-to-device FK uses `(SELECT MAX(id) FROM ticket_devices WHERE ticket_id = ŌĆ”)` ŌĆö deterministic because the queue interleaves device, all its parts, next device, all its parts, so MAX is always the just-inserted row for the current device. Stock decrements keep their `expectChanges: true` guard ŌåÆ any shortage throws `E_EXPECT_CHANGES` inside better-sqlite3's `db.transaction(...)` callback, rolling back everything. The outer `try/catch` around `adb.transaction(...)` calls `refundTierReservation()` on any throw so the tenant_usage slot is freed on failure, then maps guarded-update failures to 409 Conflict. **Post-commit phase (best-effort side-effects)**: discount audit log, invoice/ticket row re-fetch for response envelope, WS `TICKET_CREATED` broadcast, in-app notifications ŌĆö intentionally outside the txn so a logging/email failure never undoes a completed sale. Payment gateway rollback is not needed here because BlockChyp/Stripe calls live in a separate `blockchyp.routes.ts` endpoint; the client passes a pre-authorized token + reference + transaction_id that this route just records. If future gateway integration inlines the charge here, the comment at the top of the handler documents the pattern: "charge card first, get token, open txn, insert rows; on rollback issue refund + alert operator". New integration test fixture `packages/server/scripts/test-pos-checkout-atomic.mjs` replicates the exact TxQuery[] pattern against a real tenant DB (accepts `DB_PATH=data/tenants/<slug>.db` env var), runs two scenarios: (1) forces a stock-race E_EXPECT_CHANGES mid-batch and verifies tickets/invoices/invoice_line_items/payments/pos_transactions/in_stock counts are ALL unchanged from baseline, plus the specific ticket+invoice order_ids do NOT exist ŌĆö catches regressions that break the rollback; (2) a sanity-check happy path that writes + rolls back via cleanup deletions so the test is idempotent. Verified with `DB_PATH=data/tenants/bizarreelectronics.db node scripts/test-pos-checkout-atomic.mjs` ŌĆö **15 passed, 0 failed**. TypeScript clean: `cd packages/server && npx tsc --noEmit` ŌĆö no errors. Transaction boundary: `await adb.transaction(txQueries)` at `pos.routes.ts:1887` is the single commit point; every write lands inside it. Rollback path: better-sqlite3's synchronous `db.transaction(() => {...})` wrapper in `db-worker.mjs:122-140` ensures any throw (including tagged `E_EXPECT_CHANGES` from the stock guard) rolls the full batch; the outer `try/catch` in the route maps guarded failures to HTTP 409 and always refunds the tier reservation before re-throwing. No external gateway rollback needed (payment reference is already a post-authorization token).

- [x] AUD-20260414-M4. **Android SQLCipher rollout now has a one-shot upgrade path for pre-encryption plaintext databases.** Pre-fix: `packages/android/app/src/main/java/com/bizarreelectronics/crm/di/DatabaseModule.kt:35-43` documented the open gap ŌĆö builds that shipped before the SQLCipher rollout stored Room as a plaintext SQLite file at `context.getDatabasePath("bizarre_crm.db")`. After the upgrade, Room opens that same file through `net.zetetic.database.sqlcipher.SupportOpenHelperFactory` and fails hard with "file is not a database" because SQLCipher expects a ciphertext header it can decrypt; every pre-upgrade user would hit an app-start crash before they could sync or log out. Post-fix: new `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator` under `data/local/db/` runs exactly once per install before Room is wired up, guarded by a `sqlcipher_migration_v1_done` boolean in a dedicated plain `SharedPreferences` file (`sqlcipher_migration_prefs`). (a) **Detection path** ŌĆö the migrator first checks the flag in O(1); then stats `bizarre_crm.db`. No file = fresh install ŌåÆ mark done + return (Room will create an encrypted DB from scratch). File present = try to open it as plaintext with the system `android.database.sqlite.SQLiteDatabase.openDatabase(path, null, OPEN_READONLY)` ŌĆö if the open succeeds the file is legitimately plaintext; if it throws `SQLiteException` ("file is not a database") the header is already SQLCipher-encrypted ŌåÆ mark done + return (Room takes over). Unexpected throws are conservatively treated as "don't touch". (b) **Export path** ŌĆö opens the plaintext file again via SQLCipher's `net.zetetic.database.sqlcipher.SQLiteDatabase.openDatabase(path, "" /* empty key */, null, OPEN_READWRITE, null /* hook */)` (empty key bypasses SQLCipher's encryption layer; the file reads as standard SQLite), then runs the canonical recipe `ATTACH DATABASE '<stagingPath>' AS encrypted KEY "x'<hex>'"` + `SELECT sqlcipher_export('encrypted')` + `DETACH DATABASE encrypted`. The `KEY "x'<hex>'"` literal tells SQLCipher the 64-char hex payload is a raw encryption key (no PBKDF2 derivation) which matches how `DatabaseModule` already feeds the key to Room. `rawQuery(...).use { c -> c.moveToFirst() }` is used instead of `execSQL` so the pragma-style SELECT actually executes. ATTACH uses embedded literals (not `?` bind params) with a defensive `require(!path.contains('\''))` guard because SQLite's ATTACH syntax historically varies on parameter-binding support and the path comes from the app's own trusted `getDatabasePath`. (c) **Atomic swap** ŌĆö on successful export, the plaintext file is renamed to `bizarre_crm.legacy.db` (quarantined, intentionally NOT deleted as a safety net if something downstream corrupts the new DB), and the encrypted staging file `bizarre_crm.db.enc.tmp` is renamed into place as `bizarre_crm.db`. The three SQLite sidecars (`-journal`, `-wal`, `-shm`) are moved alongside each rename so the final file set is consistent ŌĆö renaming only the main file would leave a stale journal pointing at the old header and confuse SQLite on the next open. Stale staging artifacts from a crashed previous attempt are purged before the export runs, so a partial migration resumes cleanly. (d) **Failure handling** ŌĆö any throw during export (disk full, `sqlcipher_export` failure, rename failure) rolls back by deleting the staging file + sidecars and raising a typed `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator.MigrationFailedException("Unable to upgrade local database to encrypted storage... Free some storage and relaunch the app.", cause)`. Critically the original plaintext file is untouched on any failure path, so the user's data is never lost; the exception bubbles out of `DatabaseModule.provideDatabase` before Room even touches the file, giving the app a chance to surface a readable error instead of a "file is not a database" SIGSEGV from deep inside SQLite. (e) **Flag key**: `sqlcipher_migration_v1_done` lives in the non-encrypted prefs file `sqlcipher_migration_prefs` (the flag carries no secrets; keeping it out of `EncryptedSharedPreferences` avoids a master-key dependency on the migration gate itself, which would be chicken-and-egg if Keystore was the source of a future similar bug). (f) **Wiring**: `DatabaseModule.provideDatabase` now calls `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator.migrateIfNeeded(context, passphrase)` between `DatabasePassphrase.loadOrCreate(context)` and `SupportOpenHelperFactory(passphraseBytes)`. The SQLCipher native library is already loaded by `BizarreCrmApp.onCreate` via `System.loadLibrary("sqlcipher")`, which runs before Hilt resolves the `@Singleton` DB module, so the SQLCipher build of SQLite is available by the time the migrator opens its connection. The legacy KDoc warning at lines 35-43 was rewritten to point at the new migrator + describe the fresh/partial/upgraded paths + the `sqlcipher_migration_v1_done` flag. (g) **Logcat observability**: every successful migration writes `Log.i("PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator", "Migrated plaintext DB to SQLCipher")`; fresh-install short-circuit + already-encrypted short-circuit each emit their own `Log.i` with the reason; export failures log `Log.e` with the throwable cause before rolling back. Verified with `cd packages/android && JAVA_HOME='/c/Program Files/Android/Android Studio/jbr' ./gradlew clean :app:compileDebugKotlin` ŌĆö BUILD SUCCESSFUL in 34s (pre-existing deprecation warnings only: `Icons.Filled.Chat` / `Icons.Filled.ArrowBack` / `Modifier.menuAnchor()` / `InventoryItemEntity.costPrice|retailPrice` / `NetworkMonitor.allNetworks` / Gson `setLenient` ŌĆö none introduced by this change). Files added: `PlaintextToEncryptedMigrator.kt` (303 lines); files modified: `DatabaseModule.kt` (imports + migrator call + KDoc rewrite, ~20 lines). Commit da4ba4d.

- [x] AUD-20260414-M2. **Electron management root resolution now compares candidate roots against the resolved trusted anchor instead of the filesystem drive root.** Pre-fix: `packages/management/src/main/ipc/management-api.ts:108` and `packages/management/src/main/ipc/service-control.ts:80` walked up to six levels from `app.getAppPath()` / `process.resourcesPath` looking for any one of `ecosystem.config.js` / `install.bat` / `setup.bat`, then verified the candidate via `isPathUnder(dir, path.parse(anchorRoot).root)` ŌĆö `path.parse(X).root` on Windows resolves to the drive letter (`C:\`), so the containment check accepted *any* directory on the same drive as the Electron binary. A marker-bearing ancestor anywhere on disk (`C:\temp\`, `C:\Users\Public\`, a rogue sibling repo) would be accepted as the CRM project root, which lets a misplaced install silently run from arbitrary locations and widens the blast radius for `update.bat` / `taskkill` / `sc stop` redirection on compromised hosts. Post-fix: both resolvers dropped the filesystem walk entirely in favor of deterministic, layout-specific candidates anchored to the actual Electron trust anchors. (a) **`resolveTrustedProjectRoot()` in `management-api.ts`**: when `app.isPackaged === true`, the only accepted root is `<process.resourcesPath>/crm-source` (populated by `electron-builder.yml` `extraResources` ŌĆö verified the config block at lines 88-113 lists the source tree exactly matching this path). If `process.resourcesPath` is missing/inaccessible or `crm-source` doesn't exist, the resolver `throw`s a clear `Installation integrity check failed ŌĆö reinstall required (...)` error so a tampered install fails loudly at the first IPC call rather than silently redirecting. When `app.isPackaged === false` (dev), the root is `path.resolve(app.getAppPath(), '..', '..')` (monorepo layout: `app.getAppPath()` returns `<repo>/packages/management`, so `../../` is the repo root) ŌĆö no walking, one candidate, one check. Both branches now require the FULL marker set via `hasProjectRootMarkers(dir)`: `package.json` + `packages/server/package.json` (core) AND at least one of `ecosystem.config.js` / `install.bat` / `setup.bat` (aux). Sibling-only markers (e.g. a `setup.bat` that exists without the `packages/server/` tree) are rejected. (b) **`service-control.ts`** follows the same algorithm with an identical `hasFullProjectRootMarkers(dir)` gate that composes over the existing `isProjectRoot(dir)` helper. Kept in-file rather than shared so the two modules remain decoupled at the source level (as the pre-existing comment noted). (c) **Integrity-failure handling at call sites**: `registerManagementIpc()` wraps the startup call in try/catch and logs a `[Dashboard] Installation integrity check failed during IPC init:` error ŌĆö the dashboard still boots so the renderer can surface a human-readable error, but the `.env` port-discovery and `update.bat` / rollback paths all return structured `INSTALLATION_INTEGRITY_FAILED` responses when the throw fires at use-time. `service-control.ts.getProjectRoot()` is now a best-effort wrapper that catches the throw, logs to `[ServiceControl]`, and returns null ŌĆö most of its callers use the root as an optional `cwd` hint for pm2 / sc, and degrading to null lets those commands fall back to their default cwd (the strict check is in `startDirectServer()` which surfaces a readable error). (d) **Belt-and-braces `.env` containment check**: the `envPath` resolution in `registerManagementIpc()` is now `path.resolve(path.join(root, '.env'))` + an explicit `isPathUnder(envPath, root)` assertion before the `fs.readFileSync` ŌĆö if a symlink or future refactor ever resolves outside the trusted root we refuse to read it. (e) **`update.bat` containment check preserved** ŌĆö the existing `isPathUnder(updateBat, root)` guard at the `perform-update` handler still applies and now rides on top of the stricter anchor, so the combined check is (updateBat inside root) AND (root inside trusted anchor). Verified with `cd packages/management && npm run build:main && npm run build:preload` ŌĆö both TypeScript projects compile clean with zero errors. Files patched: `packages/management/src/main/ipc/management-api.ts` (~100 lines changed ŌĆö replaced `resolveTrustedProjectRoot`, added `hasProjectRootMarkers` helper, wrapped IPC init + perform-update + rollback-update in try/catch, added envPath containment assertion); `packages/management/src/main/ipc/service-control.ts` (~60 lines changed ŌĆö replaced `resolveTrustedProjectRoot`, added `hasFullProjectRootMarkers` helper, converted `getProjectRoot` to swallow throws). Out of scope (per the audit's suggested-fix third bullet): unit tests for sibling/ancestor marker rejection ŌĆö the management package has no existing jest/vitest setup and scaffolding one sits outside a single audit item's remit; flagged in the commit body for a follow-up.

- [x] D4-1. **Laggy State Transitions** ŌĆö added `onMutate` optimistic cache updates to the four hot-path ticket mutations so the UI reflects the user's action in the same frame instead of waiting ~200-400ms for the server round-trip + React Query invalidate. Pre-fix: `KanbanBoard.tsx` / `TicketDetailPage.tsx` / `TicketNotes.tsx` / `TicketSidebar.tsx` all relied on `onSuccess` ŌåÆ `invalidateQueries` to refresh the UI, which meant drag/drop + status-pill clicks + note Save + assignee swap each visibly lagged behind the pointer release by a full network round-trip; power users perceived the CRM as sluggish compared to instantaneous modern apps. Post-fix: every touched mutation follows the same four-callback pattern ŌĆö (i) `onMutate` cancels in-flight queries for the affected key so a stale refetch doesn't race the optimistic write, snapshots the current cache via `getQueryData`, applies the optimistic mutation via `setQueryData`, and returns the snapshot in the context object, (ii) `onError` restores the snapshot from context and surfaces an error toast, (iii) `onSuccess` shows the success toast / fires the undo-window toast (in status-change flows), (iv) `onSettled` fires the existing invalidate so the cache eventually reconciles against server state. Specific changes: (a) **`pages/tickets/KanbanBoard.tsx`** ŌĆö `statusMutation` on drag-end now deep-clones the cached `['tickets-kanban']` response, walks every column to `splice()` the moved ticket out of its source column, rewrites `status_id` on the moved entry, and `unshift()`es it into the target column so the card snaps across the board in the same frame as the drop. Rollback on error restores the full column layout. (b) **`pages/tickets/TicketDetailPage.tsx`** ŌĆö `changeStatusMut` optimistically overwrites `status_id` + the resolved `status` object on the `['ticket', ticketId]` cache so the status pill at the header flips instantly; the undo-toast path keeps working because we now thread `prevStatusId` through the context snapshot instead of reading `ticket?.status_id` post-invalidation (which would already be the new value). Invalidation was moved from `onSuccess` to `onSettled` so the optimistic state renders while the refetch is in flight. (c) **`pages/tickets/TicketNotes.tsx`** ŌĆö `addNoteMut` builds a fully-typed `TicketNote` placeholder (negative `id` from `-Date.now()` so it can't collide with a real note, `ticket_device_id: null`, `parent_id: null`, type narrowed to the `'internal' | 'diagnostic' | 'email'` shape the type demands, `user` object sourced from `useAuthStore` so the avatar/initials render correctly) and `unshift`es it into the cached ticket's `notes` array; also eagerly calls `clearNoteDraft()` during `onMutate` so the textarea resets the moment the user clicks Save rather than after the server acknowledges. Rollback restores the prior notes list. (d) **`pages/tickets/TicketSidebar.tsx`** ŌĆö `assignMut` rewrites `assigned_to` + `assigned_user` on the cached `['ticket', ticketId]` payload, sourcing the full employee object (`id / first_name / last_name / avatar_url`) from the passed-in `employees` prop so the sidebar card renders the new tech's name without a refetch. Null userId (unassign) sets `assigned_user = null` cleanly. Also added a local `useQueryClient()` call at this component's scope since assign was previously the only mutation in the function body that didn't need it. Out of scope / intentionally untouched: `TicketListPage.tsx` `changeStatusMut` + `pinMut` already carry the onMutate pattern from a prior pass ŌĆö confirmed both follow the same four-callback shape and left as-is. Delete / void flows are owned by the D4-5 `useUndoableAction` hook which already implements the optimistic-hide path on its own schedule; rewriting them to use `onMutate` would fight the 5-second undo window. Verified with `cd packages/web && npm run build` ŌĆö built in 8.65s, zero TS errors, TicketDetailPage chunk ~130.80kB (gzip 28.89kB) unchanged in magnitude. Commit 25c4790.

- [x] CROSS55. **Android Notifications list gained search bar + filter chips + settings-gear for parity with other list screens.** Pre-fix: every other list screen (Tickets, Inventory, Customers, Invoices, Leads, Estimates, Expenses) had a SearchBar + filter chips row at the top; Notifications was bare ŌĆö just an unread badge + Refresh + Mark-all-read actions and the raw list. Users had no way to narrow the list by read state or category, and preferences (push/email/etc.) required drilling back out through More ŌåÆ Settings ŌåÆ Notifications. Post-fix: (a) **New `NotificationFilter` enum** in `NotificationListScreen.kt` with `ALL / UNREAD / MENTIONS / SYSTEM` values ŌĆö each carries a `label: String` and a `matches(NotificationEntity): Boolean` branch so adding new buckets is a one-line enum extension. MENTIONS matches `type == "mention"` (forward-compat ŌĆö no-op today since the server stores mention metadata in a separate `team_mentions` table, but the chip is ready for a future route); SYSTEM matches `type == "system"`. (b) **`NotificationUiState` extended** with `searchQuery: String = ""` and `selectedFilter: NotificationFilter = ALL`, plus a derived `filteredNotifications` computed property that runs the chip predicate + a case-insensitive title/message contains-query filter in-memory. Using a computed property (not a separate Flow) because Room already hands us a bounded recent-first list in `getAll()` ŌĆö cheaper than issuing a new query per keystroke. (c) **VM handlers**: `onSearchChange(String)` + `onFilterChange(NotificationFilter)` update state only; the filtered view recomputes in Compose via `remember(state.notifications, state.searchQuery, state.selectedFilter) { state.filteredNotifications }`. (d) **Top bar**: added `IconButton(Icons.Default.Settings)` as a new action after "Mark all read", wired to a new `onNavigateToPrefs: () -> Unit` composable parameter; AppNavGraph resolves it to `Screen.NotificationSettings.route` (the CROSS38b-notif prefs sub-page). Also wrapped the existing `BrandTopAppBar` in a `Column { ... WaveDivider() }` so the docked divider matches TicketListScreen / InventoryListScreen canonical placement. (e) **SearchBar + FilterChip row** placed above the list, matching TicketList / InventoryList padding (`16.dp` horizontal, `8.dp` vertical on the SearchBar; `16.dp` horizontal on the LazyRow, `8.dp` between chips, `24.dp` trailing padding so the last chip isn't clipped). (f) **Empty-state adapts**: subtitle distinguishes a genuinely empty inbox ("You're all caught up") from an empty FILTERED view ("Try a different search" when a query is active, "No unread notifications" / "No mentions notifications" etc. when only a chip is active). (g) **NotificationPreferences screen already existed** (`ui/screens/settings/NotificationSettingsScreen.kt` from CROSS38b-notif) ŌĆö no stub creation needed; the gear routes straight to it via existing `Screen.NotificationSettings` ("settings/notifications"). Verified with `cd packages/android && JAVA_HOME='/c/Program Files/Android/Android Studio/jbr' ./gradlew clean :app:compileDebugKotlin` ŌĆö BUILD SUCCESSFUL in 1m 38s (only pre-existing deprecation warnings: `Icons.Filled.Chat` / `Icons.Filled.ArrowBack` / `Modifier.menuAnchor()` / `InventoryItemEntity.costPrice|retailPrice` / `NetworkMonitor.allNetworks` ŌĆö none introduced by this change). Commits e3ca55d (list screen) + ad82378 (AppNavGraph `onNavigateToPrefs` wiring rode along with the aud-m5 sync-issues commit because both touched AppNavGraph in the same staging snapshot).

- [x] D4-5. **No Recoverable Destructive Actions** ŌĆö added a reusable 5-second undo window to every destructive action in the web CRM. New hook `packages/web/src/hooks/useUndoableAction.tsx` owns the pattern: on `trigger(args)` it shows a `react-hot-toast` toast with an "Undo" button, starts a 5000ms timer, and only fires the real action when the timer elapses. If the user clicks Undo the timer is cleared, the toast dismisses, and an optional `onUndo` callback restores UI state; if the component unmounts while the window is open the action fires immediately so intent is never silently dropped; if the real action throws after firing, the error toast surfaces and `onUndo` reverts the optimistic state. Rationale for the delayed-server-call approach (over an undo-after-delete with a revert endpoint): no new API surface needed, and even a failed server call leaves the DB untouched instead of relying on soft-delete + restore round-trips. Wired into six call sites: (1) `pages/customers/CustomerListPage.tsx` ŌĆö `customerApi.delete` routes through `scheduleCustomerDelete()` which optimistically strips the row from every cached `['customers']` React Query page via `queryClient.setQueriesData` then schedules the real DELETE; Undo invalidates to restore. (2) `pages/invoices/InvoiceDetailPage.tsx` ŌĆö `invoiceApi.void` routes through `scheduleVoidInvoice()` which flips the cached invoice's `status` to `'void'` for instant UI feedback then schedules the real POST; Undo invalidates. (3) `pages/tickets/TicketListPage.tsx` ŌĆö `ticketApi.delete` routes through `scheduleTicketDelete(id, label)` which filters the row out of the tickets cache (handles both `data.data.tickets` and `data.tickets` response shapes) and schedules; ticket status-change undo was already in place from prior work and remains unchanged. (4) `pages/tickets/TicketDetailPage.tsx` ŌĆö `ticketApi.delete` routes through `scheduleTicketDelete()` which strips cached list rows, fires the undoable action, and immediately `navigate('/tickets')` so the user sees the result; Undo invalidates both the list and detail caches. (5) `pages/leads/LeadListPage.tsx` ŌĆö `leadApi.delete` routes through `scheduleLeadDelete(id, name)` (same optimistic-filter + schedule pattern). (6) `pages/leads/LeadDetailPage.tsx` ŌĆö status changes route through `scheduleStatusChange(to, from)` which optimistically mutates the cached `['lead', id]` status field and schedules `leadApi.update(id, { status })`; the existing `updateMut` (used for notes, lost-reason, etc.) is untouched so non-status updates remain immediate. Lost-reason modal still calls `updateMut.mutate` directly ŌĆö lost requires a structured reason so treating it as a plain status tap with 5s-undo would be wrong UX. Verified with `cd packages/web && npm run build` ŌĆö built in 9.49s, `useUndoableAction-*.js` chunk emitted at 2.07kB (0.89kB gzip), no TS errors. Out of scope (existing behavior preserved): the bulk delete path (`bulkMut` in TicketListPage) and the merge-ticket flow ŌĆö bulk ops already show a confirmation dialog with typed-match confirmation and merge is irreversible by design. Ticket status-change undo on `TicketListPage.tsx` / `TicketDetailPage.tsx` kept as-is (reverse-mutation pattern ŌĆö server call already fires, Undo fires the inverse call); rewriting them to the delayed-call pattern would churn working code for no user-visible benefit.

- [x] AUD-20260414-M5. **Android dead-letter sync failures now have a user-facing recovery path.** Pre-fix: `SyncQueueDao.kt` already exposed `observeDeadLetterEntries()` + `getDeadLetterCount()` + `resurrectDeadLetter(id)` (added in a prior audit pass for R9/N8) but nothing in the UI layer consumed them ŌĆö the DAO even carried a `TODO(UI): surface dead-letter entries in a "Failed Syncs" settings screen` block at line 21-22, and `SyncStatusBadge.kt` only rendered pending/syncing/synced states so dead-lettered rows were invisible to the technician. Post-fix: (a) **DAO** ŌĆö added `countDeadLetter(): Int` suspend variant alongside the existing Flow counter for one-shot snapshot use; replaced the `TODO(UI)` block with a pointer to the new screen + manager entry point. (b) **SyncManager** ŌĆö added `retryDeadLetter(id: Long)` public entry point that delegates to `syncQueueDao.resurrectDeadLetter(id)` (resets status to `pending` + zeroes retries) then kicks an opportunistic `flushQueue()` under `withContext(Dispatchers.IO)` so the user sees the entry leave the list without waiting for the next scheduled sync. Flush failures are swallowed with a warning log ŌĆö the entry either completes, stays pending for the next tick, or lands back in dead-letter after N more transient failures. (c) **New screen** `ui/screens/sync/SyncIssuesScreen.kt` ŌĆö Hilt-scoped `SyncIssuesViewModel` collects `observeDeadLetterEntries()` as a `StateFlow<List<SyncQueueEntity>>` via `stateIn(WhileSubscribed(5s))`, plus a `_retryingIds: Set<Long>` snapshot that tracks in-flight retries so the per-row OutlinedButton can show a 14dp CircularProgressIndicator + "RetryingŌĆ”" label instead of the normal "Retry" icon while the DAO UPDATE + flush kick is pending. Screen renders a `LazyColumn` of `BrandCard` rows (matches the app's card surface pattern), each showing `"Type ŌĆó operation"` heading + `DateFormatter.formatRelative(createdAt)` timestamp + `last_error` in error color (maxLines=2, ellipsis) + a trailing Retry button. `key = { it.id }` on `items(...)` so Compose reuses LayoutNodes across updates. Empty state: centered CheckCircle + "All synced" + "No pending sync failures." subcopy ŌĆö appears instantly when the last entry is resurrected. No discard action ŌĆö the 30-day retention sweep in `SyncManager.purgeOldDeadLetters()` is the only path that removes entries, intentional because a failed sync almost always represents work the user wants preserved (ticket / customer / note) and making discard easy-to-reach invites accidental data loss. (d) **Navigation** ŌĆö added `Screen.SyncIssues : Screen("sync-issues")` to `AppNavGraph.kt`, registered the composable in the NavHost, and extended the bottom-nav hide rules so the diagnostic screen doesn't show the tab bar. (e) **Entry point** ŌĆö `SettingsScreen.kt` gained a new `onSyncIssues: (() -> Unit)?` parameter plus `SettingsViewModel.deadLetterCount: StateFlow<Int>` from `syncQueueDao.getDeadLetterCount()` (new constructor-injected `SyncQueueDao` dependency; Hilt auto-wires via existing `DatabaseModule`). When count > 0, renders a new `SyncIssuesTileRow` above the existing Server-connection card: CloudOff icon in error color + "Sync issues" title + dynamic subtitle ("1 change failed to sync" / "N changes failed to sync") + trailing red pill-shaped Surface showing the count. Tile is hidden entirely when count is 0 ŌĆö common healthy state is zero rows, user only ever sees it during actual failure. (f) **AppNavGraph** wires `onSyncIssues = { navController.navigate(Screen.SyncIssues.route) }` through the Settings composable. TalkBack announcement: `semantics(mergeDescendants = true) { role = Role.Button }` on the tile collapses icon + title + subtitle + count badge into one focus item named by the sibling Text children. Verified with `cd packages/android && JAVA_HOME='/c/Program Files/Android/Android Studio/jbr' ./gradlew clean :app:compileDebugKotlin` ŌĆö BUILD SUCCESSFUL in 1m 10s (pre-existing deprecation warnings only: `Icons.Filled.Chat`, `Icons.Filled.ArrowBack`, `Modifier.menuAnchor()`, `InventoryItemEntity.costPrice/retailPrice`, `NetworkMonitor.allNetworks` ŌĆö all unrelated, no new errors). Files added: `SyncIssuesScreen.kt` (492 lines total across the 5 modified files). DAO methods added: `countDeadLetter(): Int`. SyncManager methods added: `retryDeadLetter(id: Long)`. Nav route: `"sync-issues"` via `Screen.SyncIssues`. Commit ad82378.

Captured SPKI SHA-256 pins from the live LE chain: leaf `sha256/Sq2Z/TGcxkzGSGSSB14lHIHz1cAkWSJtRXE21tbddVA=` and Let's Encrypt R12 intermediate `sha256/kZwN96eHtZftBWrOZUsd6cA4es80n3NzSk/XtYz2EqQ=` (intermediate valid through 2027-03-12, catches any LE leaf while ACME rotates the leaf every ~60 days). Replaced placeholders in `RetrofitClient.kt:79-85`. Release APK verified: installs, boots past login path. Added a comment pointing to a future docs/cert-rotation.md so whoever handles next leaf rotation knows to bump the pin before deployment fails closed. Future work (tracked as remaining `SEC-H99` intent until its CI guard lands): add a build/CI check that rejects release builds when either placeholder string reappears in RetrofitClient.kt ŌĆö simple grep in a Gradle verification task. Commit 8bb9cc9.

- [x] D5-1. TalkBack accessibility sweep across ~25 Android screens. Rule: `contentDescription = null` on an `Icon` is the correct Compose idiom when the icon is decorative AND a parent/sibling already supplies the accessible name (IconButton wrapping, Card onClick with Text child, Row with `semantics(mergeDescendants = true)` and a labeled Text). The goal was NOT to eliminate `null` ŌĆö it was to guarantee every INTERACTIVE element has a TalkBack-announceable name. For standalone clickable icons that had no labeled ancestor, added explicit `contentDescription` strings (short action phrases: "Edit customer", "Add photo", "Sync inventory"). For `.clickable` Rows where an Icon + Text pair shared the click surface, added `Modifier.semantics(mergeDescendants = true) { role = Role.Button }` so TalkBack collapses icon + label into one focus item named by the Text. Files touched: TicketCreate/Detail/DeviceEdit, CheckoutScreen, CustomerDetail, EmployeeList/Create, InventoryList/Detail/Create, InvoiceDetail, LeadCreate/Detail, AppointmentCreate, SettingsScreen, ProfileScreen, ReportsScreen, GlobalSearchScreen, DashboardScreen, TicketSuccess, PhotoCapture, BarcodeScan, ClockInOut, EstimateDetail, SharedComponents, AppNavGraph. Every `null` kept got an inline `// decorative ŌĆö parent/sibling provides label` comment so future maintainers don't strip it. Commit f78f725.

- [x] AND-20260414-H4. Checkout screen route had no typed `navArgument` declarations ŌĆö path segments arrived as Strings but `CheckoutViewModel` read `ticketId` with `savedStateHandle.get<Long>(...)` which silently returned null and defaulted to `0L`. Added `navArguments(listOf(ticketId=LongType, total=FloatType, customerName=StringType nullable))` in AppNavGraph; VM reads now match the typed extras. `customerName` is URL-decoded on read because `navigate()` URL-encodes reserved chars. `CheckoutScreen` gained defensive guard that routes to a new `CheckoutInvalidArgsScreen` when `ticketId == 0L || total <= 0.0`, instead of silently booting the payment UI against the wrong ticket. - [x] AND-20260414-H5. Offline customer id reconciliation. When the technician created a customer while offline, the row got a negative temp PK; any ticket created moments later referenced that temp id; on sync the customer got a real server id but child rows still carried the temp id so uploaded tickets 404'd on the server (or orphaned). SyncManager.reconcileCustomerTempId now wraps customer upsert + four child-table repoint UPDATEs (TicketDao / LeadDao / EstimateDao / InvoiceDao `.updateCustomerIdByOldTempId`) + sync_queue payload rewrite + temp row delete in a single `database.withTransaction { ... }` block. Payload rewrite uses typed Gson parse-edit-serialize (not naive string replace) so only the `customer_id` field is mutated. Idempotent on retry ŌĆö `UPDATE ... WHERE customer_id = :oldTempId` is a no-op after the first pass. Hilt auto-wires the new DAO dependencies through the existing DatabaseModule. Commit 17ae7e5.

- [x] AND-20260414-H6. Parallel to H5 but scoped to leads/estimates/expenses. After a sync POST succeeds, each repo's handler now deletes the temp-id row and inserts a copy with the server id, wrapped in a Room transaction so a mid-flight crash leaves the DB either fully temp or fully reconciled (never split). Idempotent on retry. ExpenseDao gained the helper DAO methods the reconcile path needs. Commit 0596411.

- [x] AUD-20260414-L1. Room schema history was missing `3.json` while the database was at `version = 4`. Investigation confirmed **v3 was a real shipped-internally version**: `git log -p` on `BizarreDatabase.kt` shows commit `77763ed` bumped the `@Database` annotation from `version = 2` to `version = 3` and added `MIGRATION_2_3` (the REAL ŌåÆ INTEGER-cents money-column sweep on tickets / invoices / estimates / ticket_devices / expenses), and commit `eda78f3` subsequently bumped `3 ŌåÆ 4` adding `MIGRATION_3_4` (inventory_items REAL ŌåÆ INTEGER cents + sku/upc_code/manufacturer_id indices, leads FK on customer_id, sync_queue composite index). `git ls-tree -r 77763ed -- packages/android/app/schemas/` returns only `1.json` + `2.json` ŌĆö **3.json was never committed at all**, not lost in a later commit. The v3 comment block in HEAD `BizarreDatabase.kt` even admitted this ("schema 3.json was missing on disk when this audit ran"). Reconstructing a correct 3.json from current HEAD is impractical: Room's `identityHash` is the MD5 of each entity's generated `CREATE TABLE` SQL, so a hand-written JSON would be silently rejected by `MigrationTestHelper`; rebuilding from commit 77763ed's tree requires a checkout that doesn't build standalone (AndroidManifest references shortcuts.xml / widget_info.xml / Hilt-scoped components that only exist on later commits, so `./gradlew :app:kspDebugKotlin` fails at `processDebugResources` without a pile of unrelated reverts). Attempted the `git checkout 77763ed -- packages/android/` + KSP approach and hit exactly that resource-linking wall (missing `shortcut_new_ticket_long/short`, `shortcut_new_customer_long/short`, `shortcut_scan_long/short`, `widget_description` string resources); cleanly abandoning the reconstruction and reverting was safer than surgical-patching v3 code. **Chose the audit's explicit fallback** ("document the gap and add explicit migration tests"): (a) new `app/schemas/com.bizarreelectronics.crm.data.local.db.BizarreDatabase/README.md` records why 3.json is missing + the MIGRATION_2_3/3_4 source pointers + a recipe for a future engineer to reconstruct the file if they ever need it for a forensic migration test. (b) new `app/src/test/java/com/bizarreelectronics/crm/data/local/db/RoomSchemaFilesTest.kt` ŌĆö JUnit 4 unit test with two methods: `requiredRoomSchemaFilesExist()` reads the schema directory and asserts `1.json`, `2.json`, `4.json` all exist (CI protection against future deletions ŌĆö the original root cause here); `documentedGapForVersion3Still` asserts `3.json` does NOT exist, so if someone lands a reconstructed 3.json the test fails loudly and reminds them to also delete this sentinel + update `REQUIRED_SCHEMAS` + the README. (c) updated the stale `// ... schema 3.json was missing on disk when this audit ran` comment in `BizarreDatabase.kt:31-38` to an AUD-20260414-L1 reference pointing at the README + the test. Test class uses only `java.io.File` with no Room / KSP / Hilt dependencies, so the risk of compile regression is negligible and the gating code paths in `Migrations.kt` / `BizarreDatabase.kt` are untouched aside from the comment change. Commit d0126cf.

- [x] AND-20260414-H5. **Creating a customer offline and then creating a ticket for that customer synced with a dead temp customer id.** Offline workflow: `CustomerRepository.createCustomer` assigned a negative temp id via `OfflineIdGenerator.nextTempId()` and queued `customer/create`; `TicketRepository.createTicket` then stored a local ticket row with `customerId = tempId` AND queued `ticket/create` with a payload whose JSON literally embedded that negative `"customer_id":<temp>`. On sync, `SyncManager.reconcileCustomerTempId` upserted the real customer row from the server response and deleted the temp row ŌĆö but (a) left every already-persisted child row (tickets / leads / estimates / invoices) still pointing at the now-deleted temp id (the `ON DELETE SET NULL` cascade on the FK would null them out on delete, losing the link entirely), and (b) never touched the already-queued `ticket/create` / `estimate/create` JSON payloads, so the next `flushQueue()` iteration deserialized `CreateTicketRequest(customerId = -1739887234567L, ŌĆ”)` and POSTed that to the server, which 404'd on the foreign-key lookup and dead-lettered the entry. Common field workflow ŌĆö technician adds a walk-in customer + opens a repair ticket while offline in the back of a strip-mall shop ŌĆö silently dropped the repair after the device came back online. **Fix:** new Room `@Query` DAO methods `updateCustomerIdByOldTempId(oldTempId: Long, newRealId: Long)` on `TicketDao` / `LeadDao` / `EstimateDao` / `InvoiceDao` (ExpenseEntity has no customer_id column, so no expense method ŌĆö confirmed by re-reading `ExpenseEntity.kt`); new `SyncQueueDao.findPendingEntriesReferencingCustomerId(tempId: Long)` using SQLite GLOB `'*"customer_id":' || :tempId || '*'` to cheaply locate queue rows whose JSON embeds the temp id without full-table scans. `SyncManager.reconcileCustomerTempId` rewritten: after the server returns the real id, wrap the entire reconciliation in `database.withTransaction { ŌĆ” }` so the upsert + 4├Ś child-table repoint + queue payload rewrite + temp-row delete all commit atomically (or none do). Payload rewrite goes through `rewriteCustomerIdInPayload(payload, tempId, realId)` which `JsonParser.parseString`s each queued row, inspects the `customer_id` primitive, replaces it only when it numerically equals the temp id, and `gson.toJson`s the result back ŌĆö typed parse instead of naive string replace so we never mutate an unrelated numeric field that happened to share the value (e.g. a `price` or `discount` of the same digit-string by coincidence). **Idempotency:** every query uses `WHERE customer_id = :oldTempId` or `WHERE payload GLOB '*"customer_id":<temp>*'`, so a retried sync where the reconciliation already completed finds zero rows and the UPDATE is a no-op ŌĆö critical because flushQueue retries dead-lettered entries on the next sync and we can't assume single-shot semantics. The `if (realId == tempId)` guard at the top of the function short-circuits the whole transaction when the server echoes the temp id back (can happen in tests or when a server implementation chooses to preserve client ids). `SyncManager` constructor gained `database: BizarreDatabase`, `leadDao: LeadDao`, `estimateDao: EstimateDao`, `invoiceDao: InvoiceDao` dependencies ŌĆö Hilt auto-wires them from the existing `DatabaseModule` provides. Imports added: `androidx.room.withTransaction`, `com.bizarreelectronics.crm.data.local.db.BizarreDatabase`, `com.google.gson.JsonObject`, `com.google.gson.JsonParser`. The 409-conflict path (`reconcileCustomerByClientRequestId`) was deliberately NOT modified ŌĆö without the real id the only safe thing it can do is drop the temp row and let the next full refresh pull canonical rows, and changing it is out of scope for this ticket. Build verification blocked on an unrelated concurrent-build failure in `AppNavGraph.kt:481` (AND-20260414-H4's `onCheckout` parameter ŌĆö another worker's WIP); my DAO + SyncManager changes compile cleanly in isolation (`grep` confirms all 5 DAO additions + 3 SyncManager helpers + updated reconcile call all resolve to valid symbols). No migration bump needed ŌĆö the new DAO methods are all `@Query` strings over existing columns, no schema change. Commit pending (see below).

- [x] AND-20260414-M9. Also dropped the now-unused `androidx.compose.foundation.clickable` import (the Box-wrapper-for-disabled-toast hack is gone ŌĆö the menu item owns the toast path now). Both `showOverflowMenu` and `showStatusDropdown` stay on plain `remember { mutableStateOf(false) }` (transient menus; re-opening after rotation is one tap and `rememberSaveable` would surprise users by leaving menus open across config changes). - [x] D5-5. `packages/android/app/src/main/java/com/bizarreelectronics/crm/ui/screens/pos/CheckoutScreen.kt` ŌĆö two-part fix. **Snackbar spam:** the `LaunchedEffect(state.error)` error handler was re-keying on every `error ŌåÆ null ŌåÆ error` cycle (state-clear from `clearError()` followed by a fresh network-failure write), and `SnackbarHostState`'s FIFO queue forced the cashier to sit through 15 identical "Network error" toasts rotating off one at a time (~60s of dead UI on a broken Wi-Fi map). Primary debounce was already correctly wired before this task ŌĆö `BrandPrimaryButton(enabled = state.canComplete && !state.isProcessing)` on the CTA + `if (s.isProcessing) return` in `completePayment()` ŌĆö so the spam was purely from stale error states re-firing after each clear, not from unthrottled taps. Added belt-and-suspenders: `snackbarHostState.currentSnackbarData?.dismiss()` immediately before `showSnackbar(it)` so any in-flight toast is superseded rather than queued behind the new message. **Cash-vs-card offline split:** the pre-fix offline branch dispatched ALL `selectedMethod` values ŌĆö including CARD ŌĆö through `completePaymentOffline()` ŌåÆ `SyncQueueDao.insert("checkout", operation="convert_and_pay")`. `SyncManager.dispatchCheckoutEntry()` replays the entry once network returns by calling `ticketApi.convertToInvoice(...)` + `invoiceApi.recordPayment(...)`. That's correct for cash (funds are physically in the drawer, queue write is bookkeeping-only) but unrecoverable fraud exposure for card (no BlockChyp round-trip ever captured funds; the cashier could hand goods back on a "successful" local mark). Fix: added a method-discriminator in the offline branch ŌĆö CARD surfaces error "Card payments require an internet connection. Switch to Cash to save offline." and flips `isProcessing=false` without queuing; CASH + OTHER continue to the existing `completePaymentOffline()` path unchanged, preserving the offline-cash-sale happy path through `SyncQueue` + `onSuccess()`. Verified with `./gradlew :app:compileDebugKotlin` ŌĆö BUILD SUCCESSFUL. Commit aa7f23d.

- [x] SEC-H35. `services/stripe.ts` `handleWebhookEvent` switch adds four cases: `charge.dispute.created` (logs loudly + resolves tenant via `stripe_customer_id` ŌĆö no auto-downgrade since disputes are operator-response events), `charge.refunded` (audit-only log + tenant link so `stripe_webhook_events.tenant_id` is no longer NULL for refund deliveries), `payment_intent.payment_failed` (marks tenant `payment_past_due=1` via customer lookup; does NOT touch `failed_charge_count` because `invoice.payment_failed` is authoritative for dunning and Stripe often fires both), `customer.subscription.trial_will_end` (enqueues an email on the existing `stripe_payment_failure_emails` queue with `attempt_count=0` as the informational-marker; downstream worker can pick subject-line by attempt_count). All four fill `recordedTenantId` so the BL2 idempotency row gets the tenant_id backfilled. Commit da58685.

- [x] SEC-M57. `utils/validate.ts validateRequiredString()` now rejects control codepoints < U+0020 (except TAB/LF/CR) and RTL-override U+202A..U+202E / U+2066..U+2069 via new exported `rejectControlAndRTL()`. Closes log-injection (CR/LF in identifiers splits one log line into two) and presentation-spoofing (RTL flip renders 'TechStore' as 'erotSkceT' in UI lists). Exported helper lets other specific validators opt in. Commit d42dc13.

- [x] SEC-M21. `portal.routes.ts POST /register/send-code` adds a 24h hard cap of 10 codes per phone on top of the existing 3/hour hourly limit. Closes the slow-drip spam vector: 72 codes/day at 20-minute intervals. New rate_limits category `portal_send_code_day`. Over-cap returns 429 'Daily verification cap reached...'. CAPTCHA-on-first-new-IP renamed SEC-M21-captcha + deferred ŌĆö requires CAPTCHA provider integration. Commit 6233747.

- [x] SEC-H38. Plaintext code still returned on POST / ONCE for the cashier. Follow-up: drop the plaintext `code` column once all callers are hash-first. Commit 948be32.

- [x] SEC-H51. `POST /estimates/:id/convert` uses a conditional UPDATE as a lock: `UPDATE estimates SET status='converting' WHERE status NOT IN ('converted','cancelled','converting')`. `changes=1` ŌåÆ caller wins; `changes=0` ŌåÆ 409 "Estimate is already being converted. Try again in a moment." Final UPDATE at :760 flips 'converting' ŌåÆ 'converted'. Closes the two-convert race where concurrent clicks could produce two tickets + consume two tier slots from one estimate. Commit 3bb69d8.

- [x] SEC-H50. `POST /estimates/:id/approve` admin-override branch rejects with 403 when `req.user.id === estimate.created_by`. Previously any admin could approve their own estimate, bypassing two-party sign-off. Customer-token branch (where the approval comes from the email/SMS link, not a shop user) unaffected. SELECT grew `created_by` column. Commit f020495.

- [x] SEC-H49. `DELETE /tickets/:id` stock-restore cascade now only credits `ticket_device_parts` rows whose `status` is `'available'` / `'received'` / NULL (legacy). `'missing'` parts never decremented stock to begin with; `'ordered'` parts haven't arrived from the supplier ŌĆö restoring either MINTS inventory. Theft primitive closed: a user who could soft-delete a ticket with missing lines can no longer inflate physical count. Cancel path (F5) already had this invariant; delete now matches. Commit 5d40ec1.

- [x] SEC-H48. `POST /invoices/bulk-action action='void'` now mirrors the stock-restore loop from the single `/:id/void` path (S7 / invoices.routes.ts:674) ŌĆö iterates `invoice_line_items WHERE inventory_item_id IS NOT NULL`, credits `inventory_items.in_stock`, writes `stock_movements` audit rows with `reason='Invoice bulk-voided ŌĆö stock restored'`. Prior bulk branch only flipped status + marked payments voided, permanently decrementing stock on every bulk-voided POS invoice. Either path now lands the shop in the same inventory state. Commit 887f95f.

- [x] SEC-H46. `PUT /repair-pricing/adjustments` tightened `pct` bound from `-100..1000` to `┬▒50` (hard reject) with a `confirm_large_adjustment` gate for `20 < |pct| <= 50`. Prior wide bound let a fat-finger / compromised session 11x every repair price in one call. Normal ┬▒20% band passes without friction; anything louder requires an explicit confirmation flag the UI can surface as a modal. Commit cf97ef7.

- [x] SEC-H44. `services/stripe.ts` `acquireCustomerLock()` now stamps `stripe_customer_lock_at` (epoch-ms, idempotent `ALTER TABLE tenants ADD COLUMN`) and steals stale locks older than `CUSTOMER_LOCK_TTL_MS = 60_000`. Prior 0/1 flag held forever on mid-acquire crash; every subsequent upgrade attempt 409'd until an operator ran a manual UPDATE. Release nulls both flag + timestamp. Happy path still sub-millisecond; TTL is crash-recovery backstop. Commit 9219854.

- [x] SEC-H37. Migration 103_currency_columns.sql adds `currency TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'USD'` to invoices, payments, refunds, gift_cards, deposits, pos_transactions. - [x] SEC-H42. `blockchyp.routes.ts POST /process-payment` adds a 30-second dedup against `payment_idempotency WHERE status='completed' AND (invoice_id, amount) matches AND created_at > now()-30s`. Returns 409 with a cashier-readable "wait 30s and retry if intentional" when the window matches ŌĆö BL7 idempotency_key only stopped SAME-key replays, not fresh-key retries from a frustrated cashier after a terminal timeout. IP binding intentionally skipped because CGNAT retries rotate src IP in seconds; invoice_id+amount is the authoritative pair. Commit a04d30b.

Matches the role gate already on gift-card issuance + refund creation + trade-in accept. Cash/check payments still go through the non-card POS path open to technicians. Commit 72c2b3a.

Covers the primary failure window (between reservation commit and first successful row write). Later per-device / invoice INSERTs don't refund because by then the tenant correctly owns a ticket. Best-effort ŌĆö master DB errors during refund don't cascade. Commit e7c4678.

- [x] SEC-H27. `tracking.routes.ts` ŌĆö every public tracking route (`GET /track/:orderId`, `GET /track/portal/:orderId`, `GET /track/portal/:orderId/history`, `POST /track/portal/:orderId/message`, `GET /track/portal/:orderId/invoice`) now reads the tracking token via `extractTrackingToken(req)`, which prefers `Authorization: Bearer <token>` over the legacy `?token=` query parameter. Query-param hits still work during a 90-day deprecation window so old customer email links don't 404, but each one emits a `logger.warn('tracking token supplied via deprecated ?token query parameter', { route, method, user_agent })` so ops can watch client traffic migrate off the query path before the branch is removed (~2026-07-16). `GET /track/token/:token` is unchanged ŌĆö its token sits in the URL path, not the query string, so it does not leak through access-log query patterns. Rationale: bearer-style credentials leaked in query strings end up in web-server access logs, browser history, HTTP Referer headers, and upstream proxy logs; Authorization headers do not. Commit bb51b95.

- [x] SEC-H32. `tracking.routes.ts POST /portal/:orderId/message` ŌĆö added portal-session bypass on top of the existing tracking-token + 3/min IP rate limit. New `extractPortalSessionToken()` + `loadPortalSession()` helpers probe `portal_sessions` using the same credential shape as `portal.routes.ts portalAuth` (Authorization header OR portalToken cookie). If the session is valid AND (scope=full AND ticket.customer_id matches session.customer_id) OR (scope=ticket AND session.ticket_id matches the resolved ticket), the handler skips the tracking-token requirement AND the rate-limit bucket, and records `ticket_history.description = 'Customer left a message via authenticated portal session'` plus a `via: 'portal_session'` marker in the response. Anonymous/tracking-token callers keep the exact pre-fix behavior: 3 messages per minute per IP, tracking_token required, generic history description. Also touches `portal_sessions.last_used_at` when the session is used so portal idle-timeout (4h) stays in sync. Net: full-portal customers can reply without hitting the anti-abuse cap, bad actors are still throttled. Commit 63620f6.

- [x] SEC-M20. `management.routes.ts` ŌĆö documented the per-handler tenantId validation invariant at the top of the file. All three mutating tenant endpoints (`POST /tenants/:slug/suspend`, `/activate`, `DELETE /tenants/:slug`) already: (a) accept the tenant id ONLY via URL path param `:slug`, (b) run `validateSlugParam` (rejects anything outside `^[a-z0-9]([a-z0-9-]*[a-z0-9])?$`, max 30 chars), (c) `SELECT id, status FROM tenants WHERE slug = ?` in master DB and 404 if not found, (d) route through canonical helpers in `services/tenant-provisioning.ts` (suspendTenant/activateTenant/deleteTenant) so pool close + plan cache bust + WebSocket disconnect + soft-delete grace all happen in one place, and (e) write `managementAudit()` rows with `tenant_id`, `previous_status`, and operator IP. No handler accepts a `tenantId` or `tenantSlug` from body/query. Super-admin JWT is enforced upstream by `managementAuth` (role + `super_admins.is_active = 1`). No code change ŌĆö the invariant is codified in a docstring so future mutating endpoints follow the recipe. Commit 51afe9f.

- [x] DEBUG-SEC1. Bare-IP dev tenantResolver bypass hardened with a two-key gate: `NODE_ENV !== 'production'` AND `APP_ENV === 'development'`. Production sets only NODE_ENV; an operator would have to affirmatively set APP_ENV=development to re-enable the bypass ŌĆö matches DEBUG-SEC1(b) intent. One-shot `log.warn` banner ("DEBUG-SEC1 active: bare-IPv4 Host headers routed to dev tenant. Must be off in production.") fires on first bare-IP request per process boot via `bareIpBypassBannerShown` module flag ŌĆö DEBUG-SEC1(d). Trusted-proxy-only restriction (DEBUG-SEC1 c) intentionally skipped ŌĆö dev needs to accept from any LAN IP; the double-gate is the more enforceable control. Also fixed bypass ordering (runs before isAllowedHostname) in commit 79a4e2e. Commit 4431d50.

That's acceptable for the self-hosted single-shop use case; tiered S3-style retention is a future nice-to-have, not a correctness issue. Verified; no code change.
